### Critical

#### P01 — timelineItems / timelineSQL union materialized as a wrapping subquery for every browse query

- **Severity:** Critical | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:30`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:33-40`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:35`
- **Time:** O(N log N) — builds the full local∪drive union of all N rows then sorts by takenAtMs; the wrapping `SELECT * FROM (union)` forces full materialization, so no index/LIMIT can short-circuit it
- **Space:** O(N) resident — every catalogued asset returned as a full ~20-column TimelineItem struct (hash/relPath/dirPath strings dominate); nothing paginated
- **Trigger:** refreshQueries() → timelineSections() on app open and after EVERY mutating action (delete, restore, evict, import, sync, drive connect/disconnect, undo, tag-sync, metadata edit). Also PeekSource and Finder-tag full reconcile.
- **Cliff:** 100k: each refresh is a few-hundred-ms main-actor stall + tens of MB transient allocation, felt as UI hitch after every edit. 1M: multi-second beachball on open and after every action; hundreds of MB allocated per refresh, GC/ARC churn.
- **Improvement:** Stop returning all N rows: paginate the timeline (keyset pagination on takenAtMs, fetch the visible window + lookahead, target O(P log N) with P≈screen). Do NOT wrap the union in `SELECT * FROM (...)` — push WHERE/ORDER/LIMIT into each UNION branch so SQLite uses idx on takenAtMs/dirPath. Drop driveRelPath/relPath from the hot path and hydrate lazily. Cache the section structure and apply incremental diffs instead of full rebuild on every refreshQueries.

#### P02 — timelineItems() — whole-library browse fetch (UNION ALL of local instances + drive-only presence, ORDER BY takenAtMs DESC, no LIMIT)

- **Severity:** Critical | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:33`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:30`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:88`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1533`
- **Time:** O(N log N) — the outer SELECT * FROM (union) ORDER BY takenAtMs cannot use assets.takenAtMs index through the UNION subquery, so SQLite filesorts all N rows; dominant term is the N-row sort + N-row row decode into structs
- **Space:** O(N) — every catalogued asset decoded into a TimelineItem struct array held resident in AppState.sections + AppState.flatItems simultaneously (two copies of ~N items)
- **Trigger:** refreshQueries(), called after every delete/restore/evict/move/metadata edit/drive connect/disconnect/import and on every grouping toggle (TimelineView.swift:180); runs synchronously on the @MainActor
- **Cliff:** 100k assets: a multi-hundred-ms hang on the main thread after every mutation and every grouping change (visible stutter); 1M: multi-second beachball on each refresh plus hundreds of MB resident for the duplicated struct arrays
- **Improvement:** Paginate/window the browse query (LIMIT/OFFSET or keyset on takenAtMs which IS indexed) so only the visible P + buffer rows are fetched — target O(P log P) fetch, O(P) resident; or run timelineItems off the main actor and diff into the grid. Avoid holding both sections and flatItems; derive flat indices lazily.

#### P03 — CatalogIngest.ingestDriveFile — per-file knownHashes() + full presence delete/reinsert, looped per adopted file

- **Severity:** Critical | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Sync & send engines | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/CatalogIngest.swift:21 catalog.knownHashes() per file`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/CatalogIngest.swift:33 vaultPresenceRows(forVault) per file`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/CatalogIngest.swift:35 replaceVaultPresence (full DELETE+reinsert) per file`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1265 ingestAdopted loop over relPaths`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:264 replaceVaultPresence`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:481 knownHashes (SELECT all hashes into Set)`
- **Time:** O(A·(N + P)) — A = adopted/ingested files. Per file: knownHashes() loads ALL N catalog hashes into a Set, vaultPresenceRows loads the drive's full presence set P, and replaceVaultPresence DELETEs all P presence rows for the vault then reinserts P+1 rows. So each adopted file re-touches the entire presence table and the entire asset-hash set.
- **Space:** O(N + P) resident per file (full hash Set + full presence array rebuilt each iteration).
- **Trigger:** 'Adopt all' on a drive with many unknown files (DriftReviewSheet 'Adopt all'), or any flow that ingests drive-resident files one at a time. A scales with unknown-file count on a freshly-attached/foreign drive.
- **Cliff:** Adopting 10k unknown files into a 100k catalog: 10k × (100k-hash Set load + full 10k-row presence delete/reinsert) ≈ 1e9 row touches + 10k SQLite write transactions. Many-minute beachball; the presence rewrite alone is O(A·P) = quadratic in the adopted set.
- **Improvement:** Hoist knownHashes() out of the loop (compute once), and replace the per-file replaceVaultPresence with one bulk presence INSERT-OR-IGNORE for all A new rows (or a single replaceVaultPresence with the full merged set computed once). Target O(N + A): one hash-set load, one presence write.

### High

#### P04 — SemanticIndex — full embedding matrix resident in RAM + per-query full sort

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/SemanticIndex.swift:6-39`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/SemanticIndex.swift:20-22`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/SemanticIndex.swift:36`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:503`
- **Time:** Build O(E·dim) (unpack Float16→Float32, one contiguous append). Query O(E·dim) for the vDSP_mmul plus O(E log E) to fully sort ALL scores just to take topN — the sort, not the matmul, dominates ranking and is wasteful for topN≪E.
- **Space:** O(E·dim) resident fp32 = E·512·4 bytes. 100k → ~205 MB; 1M → ~2.05 GB held live for the whole session (the on-disk blobs are Float16/half that, but RAM copy is fp32). Plus a transient O(E) score array per query.
- **Trigger:** Built lazily in runSearch() whenever semanticIndexDirty (set true after every embed-drain and after import growth) → first text search after any new embeddings rebuilds the whole matrix. query() runs on every text search (300ms debounce).
- **Cliff:** 100k: ~200MB persistent footprint is tolerable but the full rebuild after each embed batch stalls the first search by hundreds of ms. 1M: ~2GB resident → memory pressure / OOM risk on 8–16GB Macs (note the prior 41GB indexing OOM in MEMORY.md), and rebuild becomes multi-second.
- **Improvement:** Keep the matrix as Float16 and use a half-precision dot (or quantize) to halve RAM. Replace the full sort with a bounded top-N selection (partial sort / heap, target O(E + topN log topN)). Make rebuild incremental (append new rows instead of reloading all E). For 1M, move to an ANN index (HNSW/IVF) or memory-mapped vectors to cap resident RAM and get sublinear query.

#### P05 — items(inDir:recursive:) and folderCounts drive-branch — GLOB path predicate + union subquery for folder navigation

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:61-84`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:70`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:101-136`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:127`
- **Time:** O(N) full scan. `dirPath GLOB '<dir>/*'` cannot use the dirPath B-tree index (leading wildcard semantics / GLOB), and because items(inDir) filters the materialized `(timelineSQL)` subquery, even the non-recursive `dirPath = ?` equality can't reach the underlying index — it scans all N union rows. folderCounts' drive branch re-runs the correlated MIN(rowid) dedupe per drive-only row.
- **Space:** O(P) for the folder's items; O(F) for the counts dictionary
- **Trigger:** Folder grid open and every recursive-toggle / folder selection (FolderGridView, AppState+FolderReorg.items(inDir:recursive:true)); folderCounts on every refreshQueries() via folderTree().
- **Cliff:** 100k assets: opening a top-level folder recursively scans the whole library each time → ~hundreds of ms lag per folder click. 1M: second-plus hang per navigation; folderTree rebuild on every mutation compounds it.
- **Improvement:** Run folder queries directly against instances/vault_presence (which HAVE a dirPath index) instead of the wrapping union, so `dirPath = ?` is an index seek (target O(log N + P)). For recursive, store a normalized depth/path-segment column or a closure/materialized-path table and query a half-open range [dir, dir+'0') to keep B-tree usability (target O(log N + subtree)). Maintain folderCounts incrementally rather than recomputing all F on every refresh.

#### P06 — structuredFilter — search filter over the wrapping union with non-indexed predicates

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/Catalog+Search.swift:10-107`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/Catalog+Search.swift:57-64`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/Catalog+Search.swift:101`
- **Time:** O(N log N) — always builds+materializes the full union then applies all predicates and ORDER BY takenAtMs. Predicates on cameraModel, favorite, rating, caption are over un-indexed columns; tag include/exclude run `EXISTS(SELECT … FROM json_each(tagsJSON))` per row (json parse per asset); people/place use IN-subqueries that are index-backed but still evaluated against the full materialized set.
- **Space:** O(N) transient (full union materialized) + O(result) hashes
- **Trigger:** runSearch() on a 300ms keystroke debounce and on every filter-control toggle (ProFilterBar/SimpleFilterBar). Effectively per-interaction during active searching.
- **Cliff:** 100k: each filter change incurs a full-table json_each + union scan → ~0.5s+ lag, sluggish filter UI. 1M: multi-second per keystroke/toggle even after debounce.
- **Improvement:** Don't filter the materialized union: filter assets/instances directly with index-backed predicates, union the surviving hashes. Add indexes for the filterable columns actually used (cameraModel; partial index on favorite/rating). Normalize tags into an asset_tags(hash,tag) table with an index instead of json_each scanning tagsJSON (target O(matches·log N) for tag filters). Apply LIMIT/keyset since results feed a paginated grid.

#### P07 — DuplicateGrouper.group — per-folder union-find over pairwise pHash Hamming

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Cull & faces (clustering/dedup) | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Cull/DuplicateGrouper.swift:18-23`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Cull/DuplicateGrouper.swift:19-20`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:260`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:265`
- **Time:** O(Σ_f n_f²) where n_f = photos in folder f (Σ n_f ≈ N). Within each folder the double loop (line 18-19) compares every pair, each comparison an O(1) 64-bit XOR popcount (PerceptualHash.hamming). Best case (photos spread over F folders of even size) ≈ N²/F; WORST case (one giant folder, e.g. a flat dump of everything in one directory, common after a Google Takeout / Apple Photos import) collapses to a single O(N²) bucket. Union-find itself is near-linear; the pairwise scan dominates.
- **Space:** O(N) — byFolder dictionary holds every (hash,value) row plus parent[] arrays per folder. Modest, but the input rows[] is materialised for the whole library.
- **Trigger:** AppState.loadCullGroups() (.duplicates → hammingThreshold 2; .similar → 6) at AppState.swift:260/265. Fires on CleanupView.onAppear AND on EVERY cullMode Picker toggle (CleanupView.swift:90 onChange) and after evictions (CleanupView.swift:211,219). A cheap UI segment toggle triggers a full re-bucket + re-pairwise scan.
- **Cliff:** A power-user (100k) or anyone whose import landed many thousands of photos into ONE folder. A 20k-photo folder = ~2×10^8 Hamming comparisons per load — multiple seconds of detached CPU on every Cleanup open/toggle; a 100k single-folder dump is ~5×10^9 comparisons → tens of seconds, Cleanup view stuck on cullLoading. Symptom: long spinner / unresponsive Cleanup mode switching at large flat folders.
- **Improvement:** Replace the O(n_f²) brute-force Hamming scan with a BK-tree (metric tree over Hamming distance) or multi-index-hashing per folder: insert n_f hashes, query each for neighbours within the small threshold (2 or 6) → target O(n_f·log n_f) typical instead of O(n_f²). Since threshold is tiny and fixed, multi-index hashing (split the 64-bit hash into bands, hash-bucket exact band matches) gives near-linear grouping. Also memoize the result per (mode,catalog-generation) so a Picker toggle between duplicates/similar does not recompute from scratch.

#### P08 — FaceClusterer.cluster — greedy single-link agglomerative face clustering

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Cull & faces (clustering/dedup) | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:43-60`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:47-49`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:83-93`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:217`
- **Time:** O(n²·d) worst-case, dominant term the nested member scan × per-pair dot product. n = unassigned auto faces (personID IS NULL, source='auto'), d = embedding dim (~512-768 floats per VNGenerateImageFeaturePrint vector). Outer loop over n faces (line 43); inner loops over every existing cluster and, via members.contains (line 47), over every member already placed → in the degenerate case where most faces stay separate (singletons) this is Σ comparisons ≈ n²/2, each calling cosineDistance which is an O(d) dot product (line 88-89). So ~ (n²/2)·d float-multiply-adds.
- **Space:** O(n·d) resident. normalized[] holds every face's full unit vector (line 34-38): n × d Float = for 50k unassigned faces at d=512 that is ~100MB of Float arrays held for the whole pass, plus clusters[] index arrays O(n).
- **Trigger:** AppState.loadPeople() → Task.detached → FaceClusterer.cluster (AppState.swift:217). Fires when the People view appears with empty state (PeopleView.swift:66-67) and is re-called on EVERY face mutation: nameCluster, assign/unassign/merge/rename and after each derivation drain set facesDirty=true then loadPeople() (AppState.swift:309,326,345,365,398,1513). So a full O(n²·d) recluster runs after every single person-naming action.
- **Cliff:** Power-user 100k library where face detection yields tens of thousands of UNNAMED faces (a fresh library before any naming is the worst case — everyone is unassigned). At ~20k-50k unassigned faces the detached pass takes many seconds to a minute of CPU; because it re-runs after every nameCluster, the People view feels like it hangs/respins a spinner (facesLoading) after each name, and a 100k cold library can spin for minutes. Symptom: long facesLoading spinner, stale suggestions, high CPU; not a main-thread beachball (it is detached) but a perceived hang of the People feature.
- **Improvement:** Two fixes. (1) Correctness+structure: single-link chaining (join cluster if ANY member within threshold, line 47) transitively merges A~B~C even when A and C are different people — replace with centroid/medoid linkage or a proper density method (HDBSCAN) so a face joins only if near the cluster CENTROID, dropping per-join cost from O(cluster size·d) to O(d). (2) Scaling: build the index over face embeddings once and do approximate nearest-neighbour (a vptree / HNSW / LSH over the 512-d unit vectors) → target O(n·log n·d) build and O(n·d) query instead of O(n²·d); cap the unassigned working set and recluster incrementally (only the newly-detected faces) instead of from scratch on every facesDirty.

#### P09 — Per-query EmbedStage() construction → CLIPTokenizer rebuild (parse ~49k BPE merges) + text Core ML model recompile, every search

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Derivation / ML pipeline | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:510`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:503`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:44`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:104`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/CLIPTokenizer.swift:29`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/CLIPTokenizer.swift:68`
- **Time:** O(vocab) per search ≈ 49k merge-line parses + MLModel.compileModel of the text encoder; constant in N but a large fixed cost (tens-to-hundreds of ms, gunzip + 49k dict inserts + Core ML compile) repeated per query
- **Space:** Transient: full encoder dict (~49k entries) + bpeRanks (~49k) + compiled text model rebuilt and discarded each query
- **Trigger:** recomputeSearch → debounced 300ms (SearchView.swift:55,161) on every settled non-empty query; line 510 builds a fresh EmbedStage and calls embedText, which lazily builds tokenizer + compiles text model because the lazy-load memo lives on the throwaway instance
- **Cliff:** Independent of library size — bites on the very FIRST search and EVERY search after: visible lag/spinner (hundreds of ms) between typing and results, worst on first query after launch when the model compiles cold; the runner's already-loaded EmbedStage is not reused, so the work is pure waste
- **Improvement:** Hold a single shared EmbedStage (and thus its memoized tokenizer + compiled models) on AppState/LibraryService and reuse it for both derivation and query, instead of EmbedStage() at 503/510/254/1350. Target: tokenizer parse + model compile become one-time O(vocab) at first use, then O(contextLength) per query. Same fix removes the redundant modelID-only allocations at 254/503/1350.

#### P10 — ImportRegistry.append — full-file rewrite per imported/skipped item

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Import engines | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportRegistry.swift:78-90`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportEngine.swift:97`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportEngine.swift:149`
- **Time:** O(R log R) per item (encode all R entries + sort) ⇒ O(B·R) ≈ O(R²) for a batch of B new items into a registry of R total entries; dominant term is the per-item full re-encode + atomic write+fsync
- **Space:** O(R) transient Data buffer holding the entire serialized registry built in memory on every append
- **Trigger:** Once per staged duplicate (line 97) and once per verified import (line 149) — i.e. once per item in every import batch, every import session, forever (registry is durable and only grows)
- **Cliff:** R grows with cumulative lifetime imports. By ~50k–100k cumulative registry entries a single 5k-item import re-serializes + fsyncs a multi-MB JSONL 5,000 times; the import 'verifying' phase visibly stalls for tens of seconds to minutes (disk-bound beachball), and the friend's-real-10k import acceptance case is exactly where this surfaces
- **Improvement:** Append-only fast path: byKey/byHash are already in memory for idempotency, so just append the one new JSONL line to the file (O(1) amortized, O(R) total per batch) instead of rewriting; periodically compact. Target O(1) per item / O(B) per batch.

#### P11 — pairLiveItems — Live-photo still/video pairing

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Import engines | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportSource.swift:70-85`
- **Time:** O(P²) worst case: outer loop over photos, inner out.firstIndex(where:) at line 80 is O(P) and fires for every photo that has a video partner — which on an iPhone/Photos library is the MAJORITY of items
- **Space:** O(P) (videosByBase dict + copy of items array)
- **Trigger:** Tail of EVERY enumerateItems() on every source (CameraSource:178, VolumeSource:93, TakeoutSource:56, ForeignVaultSource:65, PhotosLibrarySource:80) — runs on connect and on every re-enumeration
- **Cliff:** An iPhone with ~20k Live photos (P≈40k items) does ~40k×40k/2 ≈ 8×10^8 firstIndex comparisons → multi-second to tens-of-seconds hang the moment the device finishes enumerating, before the grid can render; PhotoKit libraries of 100k+ make it a clear beachball
- **Improvement:** Build an id→index map once (O(P)) and look the partner index up in O(1) instead of out.firstIndex; the still already knows v.id. Target O(P).

#### P12 — Synchronous I/O façade on the calling (main) actor — LibraryService is a plain Sendable class, not an actor

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:21`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1531`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:122`
- **Time:** n/a structurally, but it means timelineItems/folderTree/reconcileFinderTags/knownSizeDateKeys all execute their O(N)/O(N log N) bodies inline on @MainActor
- **Space:** n/a
- **Trigger:** Every browse/edit call from AppState and views runs on the main thread (scanAll/rescan correctly hop to Task.detached, but the read/ingest paths do not)
- **Cliff:** At 100k+ every refresh blocks the run loop for the duration of the SQL + FS work, so the cliffs above all manifest as UI hangs rather than background slowness
- **Improvement:** Move the heavy read APIs (timelineSections, folderTree, knownSizeDateKeys, binItems) off the main actor — either make LibraryService an actor or wrap these reads in Task.detached and publish results back, mirroring how scanAll/rescan already detach. Target: no synchronous whole-library work on @MainActor.

#### P13 — evict()/rehydrate()/verifyOnCanonical()/driveSource() — full vault_presence fetch + linear .first(where:) per item and per Live-half

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService+Eviction.swift:87`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService+Eviction.swift:139`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService+DriveSource.swift:10`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:277`
- **Time:** O(K · D · M_presence) — for each of K selected items (and again per Live half), vaultPresenceRows(forVault:) fetches the entire presence table for that drive and runs a linear .first(where: hash==) scan; repeated across D connected drives
- **Space:** O(M_presence) transient per call — the whole drive's presence row set is decoded into VaultPresenceEntry structs each time, repeatedly
- **Trigger:** Each evict/rehydrate batch from the selection action bar; verified-mode evict also re-hashes each drive file (separate I/O cost)
- **Cliff:** Evicting/rehydrating a large multi-thousand selection against a drive holding ~N presence rows: K full-table fetches + K linear scans → O(K·N) work, multi-second to minutes of stall on a big drive (e.g. rehydrating 5k items from a 1M-row drive re-reads the 1M-row table 5k times)
- **Improvement:** Add a Catalog lookup keyed by (vaultID, hash) — vault_presence.hash is already indexed and PK is (vaultID,hash), so a single indexed SELECT per hash is O(log M); or fetch the drive's presence rows once into a [hash: row] dictionary before the loop. Target O(K log M) total.

#### P14 — folderTree() — folderCounts GROUP BY unioned with a full recursive filesystem walk, then parent/child tree materialization

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:178`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:150`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:101`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1535`
- **Time:** O(N + files_on_disk + F log F) — folderCounts is two GROUP-BY scans over N instance+presence rows; directoriesUnder() is a FileManager.enumerator that visits EVERY file and directory under the vault root (not just dirs) calling resourceValues per entry; tree build sorts children
- **Space:** O(F) for the byPath/childPaths dictionaries + the FolderNode tree, but the enumerator transiently touches all files
- **Trigger:** Same refreshQueries() path as timelineItems — every mutation and grouping toggle, synchronously on @MainActor
- **Cliff:** Large libraries on slow/spinning or network volumes: the full-tree FileManager walk to surface empty dirs adds hundreds of ms to multi-second stalls per refresh (the FS walk visits all media files, not just folders), compounding the timelineItems hang on the same thread
- **Improvement:** Cache the directoriesUnder() FS walk and invalidate only on folder create/rename/delete (not on every photo edit); restrict the enumerator to directories only and skip descendants of leaf media dirs; ideally derive empty-dir presence from the catalog/scanner rather than re-walking disk. Target: refresh cost O(F) from catalog with no per-refresh FS walk.

#### P15 — ingestSidecars() — per-manifest-entry sidecar read + JSON encode + catalog write after every scan/rescan

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:70`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:355`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:63`
- **Time:** O(M) per vault — reads the full manifest, then for every entry does a sidecar file existence+read, a JSONEncoder().encode of tags, and an individual catalog UPDATE (one write transaction per asset that has a sidecar)
- **Space:** O(1) streamed per entry, but O(M) total file-stat/read I/O
- **Trigger:** Runs after EVERY rescan(vaultID:) — i.e. after every delete, rename, evict, rehydrate, restore, move — not just full scans
- **Cliff:** Power-user 100k+: a single-photo delete triggers rescan → ingestSidecars walks all M manifest entries and issues up to M separate UPDATE transactions, turning a 1-item delete into seconds of full-manifest I/O; compounds with the refreshQueries hang that follows
- **Improvement:** Make ingestSidecars incremental — only re-ingest the entries the scan reports as added/changed (the scanner already diffs), and batch the catalog UPDATEs into one transaction. Target O(changed) per rescan instead of O(M).

#### P16 — FolderWatcher onChange → full scanAll of every vault (not incremental to changed paths)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/FolderWatcher.swift:36`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/FolderWatcher.swift:40`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1734`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1735`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1443`
- **Time:** O(N) per fire — full re-walk + re-stat of every file in every vault, even though FSEvents delivered the exact changed paths (eventPaths) which are discarded except for the .openphoto/ filter
- **Space:** O(N + M) — same resident footprint as a cold scan (rebuilds found[], oldByPath, instances[], …) plus replaceInstances' full rewrite
- **Trigger:** Every external filesystem change under any vault root, debounced to one fire per 2s burst. Frequent during active use (copying photos in, OS touching mtimes).
- **Cliff:** ~100k+ assets: dropping a single new photo into the library triggers a 2s-delayed FULL library re-walk + full instances rewrite. 1M: every save/copy/move under the root costs a whole-library scan; sustained churn keeps the utility scan perpetually busy. Symptom: laggy responsiveness and disk activity after any file change; combines with replaceInstances to rewrite all rows for a one-file delta.
- **Improvement:** Pass FSEvents' changed paths through to a scoped incremental scan: enumerate/stat only the changed subtrees (or files), fast-path the rest from the manifest without re-walking. The watcher already receives eventPaths — forward them instead of firing a blind full scan. Target: O(changed subtree) per fire.

#### P17 — Single-threaded hash + metadata extraction (no parallelism across files)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:63`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:71`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:91`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:96`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:57`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:60`
- **Time:** O(total bytes) for hashing + O(N) ImageIO/AVFoundation extractions, all serial on one Task.detached(.utility); wall-clock = sum of per-file latency
- **Space:** O(1) per file (streaming hash + autorelease pools)
- **Trigger:** Every full scan; the extract loop runs for every NEW hash, the hash loop for every new/changed file. scanAll loops vaults serially too (LibraryService.swift:57).
- **Cliff:** ~100k photos: first-ever scan (everything new) hashes every byte and runs an ImageIO property read + AVURLAsset load per file strictly one at a time → many minutes of indexing with cores idle. 1M: tens of minutes to hours, single-core-bound, while the disk and remaining cores sit idle. Symptom: very long indexing, app appears stalled (progress only updates on the serial loop).
- **Improvement:** Parallelise hashing and metadata extraction with a bounded TaskGroup (concurrency ≈ core count, e.g. 4–8) feeding a serialized writer; hashing is I/O-bound and extraction is CPU+I/O-bound, both safe to fan out. Note memory note in MEMORY.md flags single-threaded indexing as residual work. Target: wall-clock O(N / cores).
- **Verified:** Code confirms it: Scanner.scan hashes (lines 63-85, ContentHash.ofFile streams every byte) and extracts metadata (lines 91-122, await MetadataExtractor.extract incl. serial AVURLAsset loads) one file at a time, the whole thing on a single Task.detached(.utility) (LibraryService.swift:60), with vaults also looped serially (line 57) — no TaskGroup/fan-out anywhere. The big-O is accurately stated (O(total bytes) hashing + O(N) serial extractions, wall-clock = sum of per-file latency, O(1) per-file media space via the documented streaming hash + autorelease pools); this is a genuine parallelism/CPU-utilization limitation, not an indexing/O(n^2) claim, and MEMORY.md already flags single-threaded indexing as residual work.

#### P18 — replaceInstances — wholesale DELETE+reinsert of all instances in the vault on every scan

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:142`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:470`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:472`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:473`
- **Time:** O(N) DELETE (vaultID is leftmost of PK [vaultID,relPath] so index-supported) + O(N log N) per-row upserts each touching the hash & dirPath secondary indexes; dominant term O(N log N) index maintenance
- **Space:** O(N) — the instances[] array built at Scanner.swift:134 plus SQLite write-transaction/journal proportional to rows rewritten
- **Trigger:** Every scan, unconditionally — even when zero or one file changed (the common FSEvents-driven incremental case).
- **Cliff:** ~100k instances: every trivial rescan (one new photo, or a spurious FSEvents fire) deletes and re-inserts 100k rows and rebuilds the hash+dirPath indexes inside one transaction → multi-second write stall + large WAL growth on each scan. 1M: each incremental scan does a ~1M-row rewrite → seconds-to-tens-of-seconds DB stall and large journal churn. Symptom: disk thrash and a write-lock stall after every change, disproportionate to the actual delta.
- **Improvement:** Diff against existing instances and apply only the delta: compute added/removed/changed relPaths (the manifest fast-path already knows what changed) and issue targeted INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE. Target: O(Δ log N) where Δ = changed files, typically tiny.

#### P19 — BinStore.moveToBin full bin-log read+rewrite per file, called per file by bulk repair and deletion propagation

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Sync & send engines | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:36 list()+append+writeLog per moveToBin`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:58 list (parse B lines)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:70 writeLog (encode+rewrite B lines)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:117 repairCorrupt → moveToBin`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DeletionPropagator.swift:65 propagate → moveToBin`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DeletionPropagator.swift:111 deleteDriveOnly → moveToBin`
- **Time:** O(K·B) — each moveToBin re-parses and re-writes the ENTIRE bin log (B entries). Propagating/repairing K files into a bin that already holds B items is K·B. Compounds with the manifest cost in repairCorrupt: that path is O(R·(M+B)).
- **Space:** O(B) resident per call (full bin item array + encoded buffer).
- **Trigger:** Every deletion propagation batch (DeletionPropagator.propagate, run on drive connect) and every corrupt-repair batch. B grows monotonically because nothing hard-deletes — the bin only ever accumulates over the library's life.
- **Cliff:** Power user who has deleted/propagated 50k photos over time (B≈50k) then propagates a 5k batch: 5k × 50k = 250M JSON ops + 5k full ~MB rewrites. Seconds-to-minutes stall on drive connect; the bin log grows without bound so this only worsens.
- **Improvement:** Append to the bin log instead of read-modify-rewrite (it is conceptually append-only: BinItem per line). moveToBin → single fsync append → O(1) per file, O(K) per batch. Or add a batchMoveToBin([entries]) that reads/writes the log once → O(K+B).

#### P20 — DriftReconciler bulk repair / restore / adopt — per-file manifest rewrite inside an N-item loop

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Sync & send engines | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:172 writeManifestEntry (Manifest.read+removeAll+write)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:84 adopt`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:93 restore`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:106 repairCorrupt`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1183 repairAllRecoverable loop`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1273 restoreAllRecoverable loop`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1256 adoptAll loop`
- **Time:** O(R·M) — R = findings repaired/restored/adopted, M = manifest entries (~N). writeManifestEntry does a full Manifest.read (parse M JSON lines) + removeAll (linear scan) + Manifest.write (sort M + re-encode + atomic rewrite) on EVERY file. Dominant term R·M JSON encode/decode + R·M-byte disk rewrites.
- **Space:** O(M) resident per call (whole manifest array + encoded Data buffer); transient, not cumulative.
- **Trigger:** User taps 'Repair all'/'Restore all'/'Adopt all' in DriftReviewSheet/ConsensusRepairSheet after a drive fails verify. R scales with how badly a drive drifted (a re-formatted/half-rotted drive ⇒ R ≈ M).
- **Cliff:** A 10k-file drive that lost/corrupted a few thousand files: each repair rewrites the full 10k-line manifest, so 'Repair all' does ~thousands of full-manifest rewrites = tens of millions of JSON ops + GBs of cumulative manifest I/O. Multi-minute hang on the repair button; at 100k it is effectively unusable (the sheet appears frozen).
- **Improvement:** Add a batch API: DriftReconciler.applyRepairs([Finding]) that reads the manifest ONCE, mutates an in-memory [path: ManifestEntry] dictionary for all R findings, and writes ONCE — O(M + R). Move the loop inside the reconciler instead of in AppState. Same pattern apply() already uses for sync.

#### P21 — BinStore.moveToBin — full bin.jsonl read + rewrite per single file binned

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Vault format, IO, sidecars | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:36`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:39`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:58`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/BinStore.swift:70`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:308`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:316`
- **Time:** O(K·B + K²) — deleting a K-item selection calls moveToBin per item; each call does list() (O(B)) + writeLog (O(B)). Because the bin grows by K during the batch, the cost is O(K·(B+K)) ≈ O(K·B + K²)
- **Space:** O(B) resident per call (full [BinItem] array + encoded Data)
- **Trigger:** Every multi-select delete (LibraryService.delete([items]) loops the group, BinStore.swift via LibraryService.swift:308), plus a second moveToBin per Live-pair video (+316). Bin grows unbounded (nothing hard-deletes — vault invariant #3), so B only ever increases until the user empties the bin.
- **Cliff:** A long-lived library where the bin has accumulated B≈50k entries: deleting 1000 photos = 1000 full read+rewrites of a 50k-line bin.jsonl → multi-second hang per delete, worsening every delete as the bin never shrinks. Restore() filters the whole list the same way (BinStore.swift:55).
- **Improvement:** bin.jsonl is append-only by nature — append the K new lines (O(K), no read, no rewrite) instead of read-all+rewrite-all; for restore, tombstone or compact lazily. Target O(K) per delete batch, O(1) amortized per item. If a single-file format is kept, batch the whole selection into one read+write: O(B+K).

#### P22 — Drive propagation of a photo move — nested loop applies the full-manifest-rewrite moveFile per file per drive

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Vault format, IO, sidecars | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:133`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:134`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:136`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:183`
- **Time:** O(D·K·M log M) — for each connected durable drive, loop over all K moved files, each doing a full read+sort+rewrite of that drive's M-entry manifest
- **Space:** O(M) resident per call (one drive manifest at a time)
- **Trigger:** Same photo-move action as above, after the Mac move succeeds — runs for every connected canonical/backup drive (off-main via Task.detached, so it doesn't freeze the UI but blocks the move's completion + the final rescan).
- **Cliff:** 2 drives connected, M≈100k, moving 500 photos = 2×500 = 1000 full rewrites of a 100k-line manifest on (slower) external/USB storage → tens of seconds before the rescan/undo record completes; on a spinning external drive the fsync-per-rewrite dominates and it can stretch to minutes.
- **Improvement:** Pass the whole rename map to a single batched VaultReorganizer.moveFiles(map:) that reads each drive manifest once, applies all K renames in memory, writes once — O(D·(M + K)). Do the on-disk fm.moveItem calls in the loop but the manifest rewrite exactly once per drive.

#### P23 — VaultReorganizer.moveFile → rewriteManifestEntry (full manifest read + sort + rewrite per single file moved)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Subsystem:** Vault format, IO, sidecars | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/VaultReorganizer.swift:96`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/VaultReorganizer.swift:97`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/VaultReorganizer.swift:99`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/Manifest.swift:43`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService+Move.swift:29`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:136`
- **Time:** O(K·M log M) — moving K files re-reads and re-sorts the whole M-entry manifest K times; dominant term K·M from K full rewrites, plus the sort each time
- **Space:** O(M) resident per call — the full parsed [ManifestEntry] array PLUS the encoded Data buffer held simultaneously during write; transient, not accumulated
- **Trigger:** Every drag-to-folder / 'Move to' of a photo selection. movePhotos loops over the selection calling moveFile once per item (LibraryService+Move.swift:29), and Live-pair partners add a second call each (+38).
- **Cliff:** Power-user vault (M≈100k) moving a 500-photo selection = 500 full read+sort+fsync rewrites of a ~100k-line file ≈ tens of MB rewritten 500× → multi-second spinner / beachball on the move. Already noticeable (~hundreds of ms) at M≈10k for a large selection.
- **Improvement:** Batch the manifest mutation: have movePhotos build the full old→new rename map first, then do ONE Manifest.read + single rewrite for the whole batch — O(M log M) total instead of O(K·M). Better still, replace the rewrite-everything model with an in-memory manifest index (dictionary keyed by path) owned by LibraryService, mutated in O(K) and flushed once; target O(K + M) per batch.

### Medium

- **P24 — Whole-table Set builders: assetHashes / knownHashes / instanceHashes / vaultPresenceHashes** (`Queries.swift:196-200`, M). Time O(N) each (assetHashes/knownHashes scan all assets; instanceHashes DISTINCT-scans all instances) Space O(N) resident — a Set of N 64+-char `sha256:` hash strings (~80–100 bytes each →… *Cliff:* 100k: a few MB and a full scan, mostly fine. 1M: ~100MB transient Sets and second-scale scans during import/sync; multiple of these may be live simultaneously during a reconcile, adding to memory pressure. *→* Avoid pulling the whole hash universe into Swift: do membership tests in SQL (anti-join / `WHERE hash IN (incoming)` against the indexed hash column, or a temp table of the incoming batch joined to assets), so cost scales with the batch (target O(batch·log N)) not the whole library.
- **P25 — distinctTags — DISTINCT over json_each(tagsJSON) of all assets** (`Catalog+Search.swift:150-158`, M). Time O(N·t) — cross-joins every asset with json_each over its tag array (parses JSON for all N rows) then DISTINCT-… Space O(distinct tags) output but O(N) transient json expansion *Cliff:* 100k: full-table JSON parse each time a filter bar appears → ~hundreds of ms stall opening search. 1M: multi-second, and runs again whenever the bar re-appears. *→* Maintain a normalized indexed tags table (asset_tags(hash,tag) with index on tag) updated on metadata writes; distinctTags becomes `SELECT DISTINCT tag FROM asset_tags` (index-only scan, target O(distinct·log)). Cache the facet list and invalidate on tag edits rather than recomputing on each appearance.
- **P26 — knownSizeDateKeys — whole-union Set of size|second fingerprints** (`Queries.swift:46-55`, M). Time O(N) — scans the full timeline union (materialized) building a String per row Space O(N) resident — a Set of N `"<size>\|<sec>"` strings held while the import grid … *Cliff:* 100k: ~tens of MB of strings + a full union scan each time the importer opens → noticeable spinner. 1M: hundreds of MB transient Set and a multi-second build, on a path the user hits routinely (plugging in a phone/SD). *→* Don't materialize the union or full Set: query `SELECT size, takenAtMs/1000` directly from assets joined to presence, or build a dedicated indexed (size, capture_second) lookup table and probe it per device file (target O(deviceCount·log N)) instead of loading all N keys into RAM.
- **P27 — pendingDerivation — assets LEFT JOIN derivation_jobs per stage, full unbounded set** (`Catalog+Derivation.swift:23-38`, S). Time O(N log N) — scans all photo assets, LEFT JOINs derivation_jobs on (hash,stage) [covered by the jobs PK], sort… Space O(pending) resident hash list — on first run pending ≈ N, so the entire library'… *Cliff:* 100k fresh import: each of 5 stages returns a ~100k-hash array per drain pass → repeated O(N) scans + large transient arrays during the initial derivation storm. 1M: each pass allocates a ~1M-string array and re-scans; combined with the known indexing memory issues this aggravates the post-import memory peak. *→* Always batch with a bounded LIMIT and loop (the runner already wants resumability), so each pass is O(batch log N) and resident size is O(batch), not O(N). A partial/covering index on derivation_jobs(stage,status) and a takenAtMs index (exists) keeps the seek cheap. Verify the runner doesn't hold the full returned array alongside the per-item work.
- **P28 — phashRowsWithDirPath — full union ⋈ phash for duplicate/similar grouping** (`Catalog+PHash.swift:15-22`, M). Time O(N) to fetch (full union ⋈ phash); the downstream DuplicateGrouper.group over these rows is the real concern … Space O(N) — every phashed asset as (hash,dirPath,value) resident at once *Cliff:* 100k: full union materialization + all rows in memory → seconds to open the cull view. 1M: large resident array and a grouping pass that, if quadratic, becomes minutes/hang. *→* Fetch phash rows from instances/vault_presence directly (skip the union wrapper) and stream them into the grouper folder-by-folder rather than loading all N at once. Verify DuplicateGrouper is bucketed (group by dirPath/prefix of dHash) so it is not global O(N²); if it is, bucket by BK-tree or dHash prefix to bound comparisons.
- **P29 — phashRowsWithDirPath — materialises full timeline UNION then joins phash; embeddingsWithTakenAt — full embeddings table scan** (`Catalog+PHash.swift:15-21`, M). Time O(N) rows but with a heavy constant: the FROM clause is (timelineSQL) = localSelect UNION ALL driveSelect, and… Space O(N) — entire union (all instance rows, ~N) plus all matching phash values pulle… *Cliff:* Stress 1M instances or multi-drive (D large) libraries: each Cleanup open re-runs the full correlated-subquery UNION and decodes ~N rows into Swift — several seconds of latency before grouping even starts, repeated on every mode toggle. Symptom: Cleanup spinner latency that scales with whole-library size regardless of how few duplicates exist. *→* For duplicates, dirPath only needs to come from local instances (cross-folder near-matches are intentionally never grouped), so query instances JOIN phash directly with an index on instances(dirPath) — avoid the drive UNION + correlated MIN(rowid) entirely → target O(N) single-pass indexed scan. Add an index on embeddings(model) for embeddingsWithTakenAt. Cache the decoded row set per catalog generation so mode toggles reuse it.
- **P30 — unassignedFacesWithEmbeddings — unindexed predicate scan returning all unassigned face vectors** (`Catalog+Faces.swift:112-123`, S). Time O(F_faces) full scan of the faces table filtering WHERE personID IS NULL AND source='auto'. There is an index … Space O(n·d) — the returned array holds every unassigned face's full d-dim vector; thi… *Cliff:* 100k library with tens of thousands of unassigned faces: decoding 30k × 512 Float16 → Float on every loadPeople adds hundreds of ms of allocation/GC churn before clustering, and the result is immediately copied again by the clusterer's normalize step. Symptom: extra latency + transient memory spike feeding an already-quadratic cluster pass. *→* Store embeddings pre-normalized (the comment in Catalog+Embeddings says vectors are L2-normalized on store — do the same for faces) so the clusterer skips its normalize copy, halving resident vector memory. Add a composite partial index on faces(source) WHERE personID IS NULL, or a boolean 'assigned' column indexed, so the scan is index-driven. Return embeddings lazily / in a contiguous Float buffer rather than per-row [Float] arrays to cut allocation count from O(n) arrays to O(1).
- **P31 — Redundant full-resolution image decode across stages — each file-backed stage decodes the same original independently** (`OCRStage.swift:13`, L). Time O(N · pixels) per stage; ~4× the necessary decode work because OCR (VNImageRequestHandler(url:)), Face (CGImag… Space Per asset (transient, serial): a full-res CGImage bitmap (tens of MB for a 50MP … *Cliff:* Time, not memory: a 100k–1M first-time derivation pass does 3–4× the strictly-needed full-res decodes. On a power-user/stress library this stretches the (already long) background pass to many extra hours; not a crash, but wasted battery/CPU and a long 'still analyzing' tail. Memory is safe because work is serial and one-at-a-time. *→* Restructure the runner to iterate assets in the outer loop and stages in the inner loop, decoding the original ONCE per asset (one CGImageSource) and passing the shared CGImage/downsampled buffer to OCR/Face/Embed. Target: 1 full-res decode per asset instead of ~4 → ~4× fewer decodes on the initial pass. Keep PHash's cheap thumbnail path.
- **P32 — drainDerivation serial whole-set drain — entire pending hash list materialized, then processed one item per Task.detached** (`AppState.swift:1481`, M). Time O(N) sequential inferences per stage (5 stages) — no concurrency across assets; each item spawns its own Task.… Space O(N) resident: pendingDerivation(limit:nil) returns the WHOLE pending set as a [… *Cliff:* Stress (1M): the up-front [String] of all pending hashes is a sizeable but survivable allocation; the bigger symptom is total throughput — single-threaded inference means the library stays partially un-analyzed for a very long time. The deliberate whole-set pull (to avoid the 4.1 starvation bug) trades memory for fairness; acceptable at 10k–100k, wasteful at 1M. *→* Process the pending set in bounded chunks (e.g. stream hashes via a cursor / LIMIT-OFFSET windows so the resident array is O(chunk) not O(N)), and run a small bounded pool (e.g. ProcessInfo.activeProcessorCount-capped TaskGroup) so several assets infer concurrently. Target: O(chunk) space and ~Pcores× throughput while preserving oldest-first fairness.
- **P33 — ImportEngine Live-partner expansion via full source re-enumeration** (`ImportEngine.swift:47-56`, S). Time O(cost of a full enumerateItems()) whenever the selection references a Live partner not already selected — for… Space O(N) — materializes the entire source listing again plus a Dictionary(uniqueKeys… *Cliff:* Selecting a few Live stills off a 40k-item phone or a 100k Photos library re-scans the entire source to find their partners → seconds-long stall before the copy even starts; repeated per batch if the user imports in chunks *→* Cache the last enumerateItems() result on the source (ForeignVaultSource already caches entries; the others don't) and resolve partners from that cached array; or have enumerateItems expose an id→item map. Target O(missing partners).
- **P34 — ImportEngine verify — whole-manifest dictionary rebuild per batch** (`ImportEngine.swift:145-146`, M). Time O(M) per batch — Manifest.read decodes the entire manifest.jsonl (every line JSONDecoded) then builds a path→h… Space O(M) resident — full [ManifestEntry] array AND the manifestByPath dictionary hel… *Cliff:* At M≈100k–1M vault entries, importing even 10 photos forces a full JSON decode of a 50–500MB manifest into RAM each batch: noticeable multi-second pause + memory spike per import; at 1M this is a real allocation hit on top of the indexing-OOM history noted in memory *→* Have rescan/LibraryService return the hashes for just the placed relPaths (it already touched those rows), or query catalog.hashPresent for the B placed paths instead of loading all M manifest entries. Target O(B log M).
- **P35 — Source enumeration materializes all items + full id→object map resident** (`CameraSource.swift:162-178`, L). Time O(N) build + O(N log N) sort by takenAt; for PhotosLibrarySource each asset also calls PHAssetResource.assetRe… Space O(N) resident and unbounded — full [ImportItem] array PLUS a parallel map held a… *Cliff:* A 100k–1M-item phone or Photos library builds hundreds of MB of ImportItem + retained PHAsset/ICCameraItem objects up front with no windowing → high memory and a slow 'Reading N of M' phase before anything is shown; combined with pairLiveItems O(P²) this is the dense-import beachball *→* Stream/paginate enumeration (yield in chunks via AsyncStream) and store only lightweight handles (PHAsset localIdentifier / ICC index) resolved lazily at fetch/thumbnail time rather than retaining full resource objects for all N. Target O(window) resident.
- **P36 — TakeoutSource.enumerateItems — single-threaded per-file EXIF + JSON probe** (`TakeoutSource.swift:36-57`, M). Time O(files) but with a heavy synchronous constant per file: bestTakenAt opens a CGImageSource to read EXIF (line … Space O(files) for the items array (bounded per-file) *Cliff:* A 50k-photo Takeout export does 50k sequential CGImageSource opens + sidecar reads with zero parallelism → minutes-long 'reading' with no concurrency win; the JSON sidecar parse is also redundantly repeated at fetch time *→* Mirror VolumeSource's bounded 8-wide TaskGroup for the EXIF/JSON resolve pass, and parse each item's Takeout JSON once (cache takenAt/geo on the candidate) so fetch reuses it. Target same O(files) work at ~8× throughput, no double parse.
- **P37 — knownSizeDateKeys() — full-union scan building a Set of size|second fingerprints** (`Queries.swift:46`, M). Time O(N) — runs the full timelineSQL union (local ∪ drive-only) and builds an N-entry Set; no index help because i… Space O(N) — a resident Set<String> with one entry per catalogued asset, held as the i… *Cliff:* 100k-1M library: opening the import sheet stalls for hundreds of ms to seconds building the fingerprint set, and holds tens of MB resident for the duration of the import session *→* Query just the two needed columns directly from assets joined to presence (no full TimelineItem union projection needed here), or precompute/persist a fingerprint index incrementally during scan. Run off the main actor. Target O(N) once, off-thread, with a narrow projection.
- **P38 — tap(index:) selection — firstIndex linear scan + orderedSelectable rebuild per click** (`TimelineView.swift:112`, S). Time O(P) per tap — state.flatItems.firstIndex(where:) is a linear scan of all P visible items, and orderedSelectab… Space O(P) transient per tap for the rebuilt orderedSelectable array *Cliff:* Power-user 100k with min-zoom dense grid where flatItems holds the whole library: a single click does a 100k-element scan + array build each time — perceptible per-click lag and GC churn once P is in the tens of thousands *→* Pass the cell's already-known index from the grid's enumeration (ForEach already has it) instead of firstIndex; cache orderedSelectable as stored @State rebuilt only when flatItems changes, or have SelectionModel work directly off ids. Target O(1) per tap.
- **P39 — updateDrag(rect:frames:items:) — rubber-band hit-test over all items per drag tick** (`SelectionModel.swift:81`, M). Time O(P) per drag update — iterates every SelectableItem and does a frames dictionary lookup + rect.intersects; ca… Space O(P) for the cellFrames dictionary published via the CellFramesKey preference fo… *Cliff:* Dense min-zoom grid with many thousands of cells active: each of 60 frames/sec scans all P items → dropped frames / janky rubber-band once P reaches ~10k-50k; the per-cell GeometryReader preference aggregation that fills cellFrames is itself O(active cells) per layout *→* Spatially index cell frames (sorted-by-Y array or grid bucket) so updateDrag tests only cells whose row band intersects the drag rect — target O(log P + hits) per tick; only publish frames for on-screen cells.
- **P40 — PresenceService.locations / isOnlyOnThisMac — per-hash multi-registry fan-out, called per item in batch deletion checks** (`PresenceService.swift:45`, M). Time Per hash: instances(forHash) (indexed) + registeredVaults() + vaultPresenceHashes(forVault) per non-local vaul… Space O(presence rows per hash) transient, but vaultPresenceHashes returns the FULL Se… *Cliff:* Selecting K=10k+ assets for eviction/delete on a library with several registered drives: each hash re-fetches registeredVaults and re-materializes each drive's entire vault_presence hash Set (O(P_vault) per hash) → O(K · V · P_vault). At a 100k-asset drive and K in the thousands this is a multi-second beachball on the delete/evict path. Symptom: UI hang when confirming a large eviction/deletion. *→* Batch the presence query: load registeredVaults and each vault's presence Set ONCE, and resolve the whole hash list against in-memory maps (or a single SQL join over the K hashes). Target: O(V·P_vault + K) instead of O(K·V·P_vault).
- **P41 — Scan is not resumable — manifest + instances written only at the very end** (`Scanner.swift:127`, M). Time O(N) work discarded on interruption; a cold restart re-hashes everything from scratch (no partial persistence) Space n/a (correctness/throughput, not a memory bound) *Cliff:* ~100k+ on first import: hashing every byte can take many minutes; quitting or a crash mid-scan throws away all hashing/extraction work, so the next launch starts over. 1M makes an uninterrupted run impractical → indexing may never complete across normal quit cycles. Symptom: repeated full re-hash, never-finishing first index on very large libraries. *→* Persist incrementally: commit assets/instances and append manifest entries per batch (ties into the batching fix) so completed work survives interruption and a resumed scan skips already-hashed files via the manifest fast-path. Target: O(remaining) work after a restart.
- **P42 — Scanner.scan — whole-pipeline resident arrays (found, aligned, newAssets, pairCandidates, instances) + manifest dict all held simultaneously** (`Scanner.swift:24`, L). Time O(N) walk + O(N) align + O(N) extract; dominant term O(N) file ops Space O(N + M) — found[] + aligned[] + newAssets[] + pairCandidates[] + instances[] + … *Cliff:* ~100k assets: several hundred MB of Swift structs + the manifest dict resident through the entire scan (each tuple carries URL + rel String + ISO mtime String). 1M: low-GB resident array footprint on top of the (already-fixed) per-file pools; sustained pressure / paging on smaller Macs. Symptom: high memory watermark and GC/paging during indexing, not a hard OOM since per-file work is pooled. *→* Stream the pipeline in bounded batches instead of materializing all assets: walk→hash→extract→persist in chunks of e.g. 500 files, releasing each batch's arrays before the next. Keep only oldByPath (O(M), unavoidable for the fast-path) resident, or replace it with a per-batch indexed manifest lookup. Target: O(batch + M) space, O(N) time.
- **P43 — knownHashes() — full assets-hash set loaded into RAM each scan** (`Scanner.swift:88`, S). Time O(N) to read all hashes; membership test is O(1) per file so the lookup loop is fine Space O(N) — a Set<String> of every asset hash (each ~71-char 'sha256:…' string) held … *Cliff:* 1M assets: a Set of ~1M 70-byte hash strings ≈ tens of MB plus Set overhead, rebuilt on every scan including trivial incremental ones. At 100k it is a few MB — wasteful but tolerable. Symptom: extra tens of MB and an O(N) read on every (even one-file) rescan; compounds the per-scan cost alongside the full re-walk. *→* For incremental scans, test newness per-hash with an indexed EXISTS query (assets.hash is PK) over only the new candidates instead of loading the entire hash set; keep the bulk Set only for true cold scans. Target: O(new candidates · log N) time, O(1) extra space on incremental scans.
- **P44 — CatalogSnapshot.import / verifyAdoption — read all snapshot assets + presence into memory, bulk insert** (`CatalogSnapshot.swift:78 AssetRecord.fetchAll (all snapshot assets)`, M). Time O(N_snap) — fetch all snapshot assets, insertAssetsIfAbsent loops one INSERT per asset, replaceVaultPresence d… Space O(N_snap) resident — full [AssetRecord] array (each with caption/tagsJSON string… *Cliff:* Adopting a 1M-asset foreign drive snapshot: a 1M-element AssetRecord array + presence array materialized in one go is a multi-hundred-MB transient spike (relevant given the prior 41GB indexing OOM history). Linear in time but a memory spike, not bounded/batched. *→* Stream the snapshot in cursor batches (fetchCursor + chunked insert with autorelease pools) instead of fetchAll → bounded O(batch) memory. Use one INSERT-OR-IGNORE with a prepared statement rather than per-row insert. Target time O(N_snap), space O(batch).
- **P45 — CatalogSnapshot.write — VACUUM-copy whole catalog + per-hash thumbnail file copies, on every sync** (`CatalogSnapshot.swift:29 VACUUM INTO (full DB copy)`, M). Time O(N_catalog + H) wall-clock dominated by I/O — VACUUM INTO copies the ENTIRE live catalog (all N assets + embe… Space O(size of whole catalog.sqlite) written to the drive each time (transient temp d… *Cliff:* 100k-asset catalog with embeddings/faces (catalog DB easily 1–5 GB): every sync, even a 1-file delta, VACUUMs the multi-GB DB to a temp on the (often slow, USB/exFAT) drive + copies up-to-100k thumbnails. Tens of seconds to minutes of 'finishing' after the copy already completed; on slow removable media this dominates total sync time. *→* Skip snapshot rewrite when the manifest hash-set is unchanged since the last snapshot (store a content fingerprint in snapshot.json); copy only thumbnails not already present (the import side already does this guard but write does not); and consider exporting only the portable assets/presence tables the reader actually uses rather than VACUUMing the full derived catalog. Target: cost ∝ delta, not ∝ N.
- **P46 — SendEngine live dedup + SendReverifier reconcile — nested membership scan with no index** (`SendEngine.swift:33 for item in items { isPresent(...) }`, S). Time Dedup is O(items·present): each of K send items linear-scans the full present[] list (no Set/dict). enumerateP… Space O(present) resident (full fingerprint array held for the batch). *Cliff:* Sending 1k photos to an SD card that already holds 20k files: enumeratePresent re-hashes all 20k files (gigabytes of reads) and then dedup does 1k×20k = 20M fingerprint comparisons. The re-hash of the whole card is the real wall — minutes before the send even starts; the nested scan adds a smaller but avoidable cost. *→* Index present[] once into a [hash: _] dict and a [(size,captureSecond): _] dict, then dedup/reverify are O(K + present). For VolumeCopyDestination, cache fingerprints by (size,mtime) so unchanged files aren't re-hashed every send. Target dedup O(K+present), enumerate amortized O(changed files).
- **P47 — SendRegistry / DeviceRegistry — full JSONL parse on init and full rewrite on every append/upsert** (`SendRegistry.swift:81 append (rewrites all entries sorted)`, S). Time SendRegistry.append is O(Sends) per confirmed send (sorts and re-encodes ALL prior send entries), so confirmin… Space O(Sends) resident — the entire send history kept in byKey and re-serialized each… *Cliff:* A user who has sent ~100k photos to phones over years: each new confirmed send re-sorts+re-encodes the full 100k-entry sends.jsonl, so a 1k-photo send batch rewrites a multi-MB file 1k times. Noticeable lag accumulating during/after a large send; the file rewrite is the dominant cost. *→* Make sends.jsonl append-only (it is idempotent by key and already line-oriented): append one line per confirmed send → O(1) amortized, O(K) per batch. Add a [destinationKey: Set<hash>] and a fingerprint index for O(1) contains/wasSentToDevice. Compact lazily, not per write.
- **P48 — SyncEngine.plan — manifest diff and conservative dest hashing** (`SyncEngine.swift:14 plan`, M). Time Core diff is O(S + Dst) — destination manifest is hashed into a [path:hash] dict once, then each of S source e… Space O(Dst) for driveByPath; per-entry sidecar Data is released each iteration. *Cliff:* First sync to a drive that already has files but no/blank manifest (e.g. manually pre-populated): every dest file gets full-hashed = O(Dst · filesize) = gigabytes of reads → multi-minute 'planning' with no progress bar. Steady-state syncs (manifest present) are fine to 100k. The 2× sidecar read per entry adds 2·S small reads even when nothing changed. *→* Gate the dest-file re-hash on a size/mtime mismatch first (cheap stat) before hashing; skip sidecar reads when the source sidecar mtime is unchanged since last sync (cache last-synced sidecar mtimes). Diff stays O(S+Dst); avoid the O(Dst·bytes) worst case.
- **P49 — BinStore.list — full parse of bin.jsonl on every call (no cache)** (`BinStore.swift:58`, S). Time O(B) read + JSON-decode-per-line on every invocation; called internally by every moveToBin/restore and by binI… Space O(B) resident — the whole decoded [BinItem] array *Cliff:* B≈50k bin entries: opening the Bin view decodes 50k JSON lines on the main path; combined with the per-item moveToBin (separate finding) the same O(B) parse happens K times within one delete batch. *→* Cache the decoded bin list in BinStore and mutate incrementally (append on bin, remove on restore), flushing append-only; invalidate on external change. Target O(1) amortized list access and O(K) batch mutation.
- **P50 — LibraryService.ingestSidecars — open + XMLDocument/XPath parse of every sidecar after every scan** (`LibraryService.swift:70`, M). Time O(M) file existence-checks + O(S) sidecars fully DOM-parsed, where each parse builds an XMLDocument and runs ~… Space O(size of one sidecar's DOM) transient per file — bounded, but the loop holds no… *Cliff:* At M≈100k with most files carrying sidecars, every post-edit rescan re-stats 100k paths and re-parses every sidecar DOM even though only the few just-edited files changed → seconds of off-main work after each move/delete, delaying the UI refresh; at 1M it dominates scan time and re-does fully redundant work. *→* Incremental ingest: only re-read sidecars whose media changed in this scan (Scanner already knows hashedCount/new paths), or skip files whose sidecar mtime is unchanged since last ingest. Replace per-file XMLDocument with a lightweight targeted parse (the schema is fixed and self-authored). Target O(changed) instead of O(M).
- **P51 — Manifest.write — re-sort all entries on every write** (`Manifest.swift:38`, S). Time O(M log M) per write — sorts the entire entry array by path on every single rewrite, even when the manifest wa… Space O(M) — sorted copy + encoded Data buffer both resident *Cliff:* Amplifies the moveFile quadratic: at M≈1M each of the K rewrites sorts a million entries. The manifest is already maintained sorted, so the sort is pure waste on incremental rewrites. *→* Keep the manifest sorted as an invariant and have callers preserve order (insert/replace in place), so write() can skip the sort — or expose a write(preSorted:) fast path. Combined with batched mutation this removes the dominant cost from incremental edits. Target O(M) write, O(log M) insert.
- **P52 — syncFinderTagsNow — per-asset Finder-tag reconcile + sidecar rewrite over the whole catalog** (`AppState.swift:128`, M). Time O(N·instances) — for each of N unique assets: resolve all instance URLs, fileExists each, read xattr each, Tag… Space O(1) per asset (bounded sets), N iterations *Cliff:* N≈100k with the toggle flipped on = 100k× (multiple stats + xattr reads + conditional fsync'd sidecar rewrites). Even off-main this is minutes of disk churn and 100k potential fsync barriers; the trailing refreshQueries lands only after it all completes. *→* Only reconcile assets whose Finder xattr generation/mtime changed since last sync (persist a per-asset sync watermark), and batch the catalog/sidecar writes. For the toggle-on case, gate behind an explicit progress UI. Target O(changed) per pass.
### Low

- **P53 — rewriteVaultPresencePaths — GLOB scan + per-row UPDATE on a folder move** (`Catalog.swift:385-412`, S). Time O(N) scan (`relPath GLOB '<from>/*'` cannot use an index) + O(matched) individual UPDATE-by-rowid statements i… Space O(matched) rows fetched into Swift before rewriting *Cliff:* 100k presence rows: a folder move full-scans vault_presence and issues one UPDATE per matched row → noticeable pause on big-folder moves. 1M: multi-second freeze during a drag-drop reorg. *→* Do the rewrite as set-based SQL UPDATEs (single `UPDATE … WHERE relPath GLOB ?` with SQL string functions, or a range predicate on a normalized path column) instead of fetch-loop-update; keep it O(matched) work inside one statement and avoid round-tripping rows to Swift.
- **P54 — FocusMeasure.varianceOfLaplacian on bursts — per-item full pixel scan, plus per-item thumbnail decode in the burst loop** (`FocusMeasure.swift:7-27`, M). Time Per image O(w·h) over a 256×256 cap = ~65k pixel ops — bounded per image. Across a burst-cull load it runs onc… Space O(w·h) transient (a 256×256 gray buffer, ~64KB) per call — negligible per call, … *Cliff:* A library with thousands of burst photos (action/sports shooters): the burst path serially fetches+decodes a thumbnail and runs the Laplacian for every burst member. With cold thumbnail cache this is thousands of sequential disk decodes → multi-second Cleanup-bursts load. Symptom: slow first open of Bursts mode; bounded but serial. *→* Sharpness is a deterministic function of the image and should be derived once and cached in the catalog (a 'sharpness' column populated by a derivation stage), not recomputed on every Cleanup open. Then KeeperSelector reads a stored Double → O(1) per item, removing all per-load decode work. Effort to add a derivation stage is M; the read-side change is S.
- **P55 — CLIPTokenizer.bpe greedy-merge loop — quadratic in token length with unbounded per-instance cache** (`CLIPTokenizer.swift:127`, S). Time O(L²) per word: the merge loop re-scans the whole symbol list (lines 143-149) to find the lowest-rank adjacent… Space Per-instance `cache: [String:[String]]` grows unbounded with the number of DISTI… *Cliff:* No realistic cliff: query words are short and few, so O(L²) is negligible and the unbounded cache can't grow because the instance is discarded each query. Would only matter if a single long-lived tokenizer tokenized millions of distinct words (e.g. OCR-text embedding) — not done today. *→* If embeddings ever extend to long machine text, replace the O(L²) scan with a priority-queue/linked-list BPE (standard O(L log L)) and bound the cache (LRU). For current query-only use, no change required. Target: O(L log L) per word, bounded cache.
- **P56 — FaceStage per-face crop + feature-print (Vision) within one image** (`FaceStage.swift:35`, M). Time O(faces · featureprint) per image: one VNDetectFaceRectangles on the full image, then a separate VNGenerateIma… Space Per face: a cropped CGImage + a feature-print Float vector; serial, transient *Cliff:* Bites on libraries heavy with crowd/event photos: an image with dozens of faces does dozens of feature-print passes. Multiplied across N assets this lengthens the faces stage; per-image it can be a noticeable per-asset stall but stays off-main. Not a crash. Medium only at large libraries with many high-face-count images. *→* Batch the per-face feature-print requests into a single VNImageRequestHandler.perform([...]) where possible, or reuse one handler over the full image with ROIs, to cut per-face handler setup. Target: amortize handler overhead; still O(faces) inferences but fewer allocations.
- **P57 — GeoNames dataset held fully resident in RAM for app lifetime** (`GeoNamesLoader.swift:46`, M). Time Load is O(G) one-time parse of cities15000.txt (~30k lines) + admin1/country dicts; reserveCapacity(30_000) co… Space O(G) resident permanently: ~30k City structs (each holds 3 String fields name/re… *Cliff:* Constant in library size (G is fixed ~30k) — a few MB resident, never released. Not a scaling cliff per the N/M/F vocab, but a fixed memory tax. Only a concern on a memory-constrained machine alongside the indexing OOM history (MEMORY.md). Low severity. *→* Acceptable as-is for ~30k cities. If memory pressure matters, lazily load only on first geocode and release after the geocode stage drains, or back the grid with an mmap'd/SQLite spatial table so cities aren't all resident. Target: O(cells touched) resident instead of O(G).
- **P58 — ReverseGeocoder.place nearest-city lookup (per geotagged photo)** (`ReverseGeocoder.swift:47`, S). Time ~O(1) amortized per photo: a 1°×1° grid bucket with an expanding 3×3→9×9 ring (ring ≤ 4), haversine only over … Space O(1) per call *Cliff:* Not a cliff — the grid index already gives near-constant lookup. Confirmed the spatial index the audit prompt asked about already exists. No user-visible problem at any modeled size. *→* Already correctly indexed; no change needed. (If anything, note the expanding-ring cap of 4° / 444km vs the maxKilometers=250 default is consistent.) Target: keep O(1)-amortized.
- **P59 — ForeignVaultSource.folderCounts / enumerateItems — manifest + snapshot fully resident** (`ForeignVaultSource.swift:24-66`, M). Time O(M) to parse the foreign manifest (cached after first) + O(M) snapshotDates which SELECTs every (hash,takenAt… Space O(M) resident and cached for the source's lifetime: cachedEntries ([ManifestEntr… *Cliff:* A 100k–1M-item donor drive holds its entire manifest array AND a full hash→date dictionary in RAM the whole time the import sheet is open; combined with the local catalog this doubles resident metadata. Visible as a slow first-list and elevated memory on large donor drives *→* Read takenAt directly off each manifest entry's mtime when no snapshot, and where a snapshot exists, join per-hash lazily (indexed lookup) instead of slurping all rows into a dict; page the entries list. Target O(window) resident.
- **P60 — reconcileFinderTags() — reads + rewrites Finder tags on every local instance file, on the main actor** (`LibraryService.swift:243`, S). Time O(instances · tag-I/O) — reads Finder xattrs from every local file of the asset, merges, then writes the merge… Space O(tags) — small, but per-call file I/O dominates *Cliff:* Not N-scaling per call (bounded by instance count of one asset), but each edit does synchronous multi-file xattr I/O + a full refreshQueries on the main thread → a tag edit on a large library beachballs because of the refresh, not the tag write itself *→* Run the xattr read/write off the main actor and decouple the follow-up refresh from a full refreshQueries (update just the edited row). Target: no main-thread file I/O on tag edit.
- **P61 — DeletionPropagator.propagate / deleteDriveOnly — single atomic manifest rewrite (verification it is NOT per-file)** (`DeletionPropagator.swift:75 single Manifest.read+filter+write after the loop`, S). Time Manifest side is O(M) total — ONE read + Set-membership filter + ONE write for the whole batch (correct single… Space O(M) transient for the manifest filter. *Cliff:* Manifest side scales fine to 100k+; the batch's real cost is the per-file bin-log rewrite (separate finding). No additional manifest cliff here — included to confirm the single-rewrite is correct. *→* No change needed on the manifest path; it already does the correct single read/filter/write. Only fix the moveToBin per-file cost (see BinStore finding).
- **P62 — DriftReconciler.walk / scan / verify — full recursive enumeration each call** (`DriftReconciler.swift:7 walk (enumerate all files, build [rel:meta] dict)`, L). Time scan = O(M) (walk + 3 sorts of findings; no hashing). verify = O(M · filesize) — re-hashes every file. verifyA… Space O(M) resident — walk holds the entire on-disk file map; scan also builds Set(man… *Cliff:* scan: a 100k-file drive builds a 100k-entry dict + sorts findings each connect — sub-second to a couple seconds, acceptable. verify: re-hashing a full 1M-file / multi-TB drive is inherently hours (fundamental, has progress UI). The held O(M) walk map is the only memory concern; bounded and released. *→* scan is already minimal (no hashing). For verify, the cost is intrinsic; no algorithmic fix. Optionally stream/parallelize hashing within memory bounds (matches the indexing memory-safety follow-up). Keep as-is otherwise.
- **P63 — SyncLog.append — read-whole-file + rewrite-whole-file per log line** (`SyncLog.swift:5 append (Data(contentsOf:) whole file + AtomicFile.write whole file)`, S). Time O(L) per appended line — reads the entire existing sync-log into memory and rewrites it atomically to add one … Space O(L) resident transiently (whole log buffer). *Cliff:* After years of frequent syncs the per-vault sync log reaches tens of thousands of lines; each sync then re-reads+rewrites the whole (MB-scale) log a couple of times. Minor today, but a slow unbounded creep — a few hundred ms per sync at the high end, not user-blocking. *→* Append to the file (FileHandle seekToEnd + write + fsync) instead of read-all/rewrite-all → O(1) per line. The atomic-rewrite guarantee isn't needed for an informative append-only log.
- **P64 — FileNaming.collisionFreeURL — linear-probe collision resolution with a fileExists stat per probe** (`FileNaming.swift:6`, S). Time O(C) fileExists syscalls where C = number of existing 'name (n)' collisions for that basename; each probe is a… Space O(1) *Cliff:* Pathological only: a directory holding thousands of files all sharing one basename stem (e.g. mass import of IMG_1.JPG duplicates) makes each move O(C) with C in the thousands; combined with the per-move manifest rewrite this compounds. Not a typical-library problem. *→* When a directory is known to have heavy collisions, snapshot its contentsOfDirectory once into a Set and probe in memory instead of one stat per candidate; or start n near the last-known max. Target O(1) amortized after one directory listing.
- **P65 — SidecarExporter.export — read every manifest entry, parse+re-serialize every sidecar, atomic-write per asset** (`SidecarExporter.swift:11`, S). Time O(V·M) — for each vault, read its full manifest, then for each entry: read+XMLDocument-parse the source sideca… Space O(M) for the manifest array per vault; O(1) per asset otherwise *Cliff:* Exporting a 1M-asset library = 1M sidecar parse+serialize+fsync cycles → tens of minutes with no incremental/resumable progress; an fsync per file is the dominant cost on the destination volume. *→* Skip the parse+re-serialize round-trip — copy the existing sidecar bytes directly when no transform is needed (the source is already valid XMP), and drop the per-file fsync (batch fsync the destination dir once at the end) since this is a derived export, not vault state. Target O(M) reads with no parse and one fsync.

### Critical

#### D01 — refreshQueries() is a synchronous main-actor full-rebuild fired from ~27 sites — main-thread hazard that scales with library size

- **Severity:** Critical | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** AppState architecture | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1531 (refreshQueries)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:88 (timelineSections)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:178 (folderTree)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:150 (directoriesUnder FS walk)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1061 (refreshPendingDeletions)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:30 (timelineSQL UNION)`
- **Problem:** refreshQueries() runs entirely on the main actor and synchronously rebuilds ALL derived browse state on every call: catalog.timelineItems() executes the full local∪drive-only UNION and materializes every row, groupedSections() is O(N), folderTree() runs catalog.folderCounts() PLUS a recursive FileManager.enumerator walk of the entire primary-vault filesystem tree (directoriesUnder), then binItems() and refreshPendingDeletions() (a loop over every connected drive issuing per-drive vaultPresenceRows/instanceHashes queries).
