It is invoked from ~19 in-class call sites and 8 view sites (videoOnly didSet, every move/delete/evict/rehydrate/rename/sync/drift/adopt/send/reverify path, plus onChange handlers in views). At the documented 10k+ import smoke this is a multi-hundred-ms main-thread stall per state change; it directly causes the known dense-grid Space-switch hitch and blocks the deferred tile-grid optimization. Because it is `throws` and synchronous it cannot move heavy work off-main without a signature change.
- **Proposed change:** Split into an async producer + a main-actor publisher. Introduce a `LibraryQueryService` (or method on a new query coordinator) that computes (sections, flatItems, folderTree, binEntries, pendingDeletions) inside Task.detached(.userInitiated) returning a single immutable `BrowseSnapshot` value; AppState (or a focused `@Observable BrowseModel`) assigns the snapshot on the main actor. Add coalescing (a generation token / debounce) so the ~27 triggers collapse to one rebuild per event loop, and make folderTree’s filesystem walk incremental or cached (invalidated only by folder-reorg ops, not by every delete/rename). Keep a synchronous fast path only for the create-folder case that legitimately needs no DB reload.
- **Risk:** Medium-high blast radius: every call site and the 8 view onChange handlers must move from `try? refreshQueries()` to an async/await or fire-and-forget request; making the result async introduces a window where views show stale counts, so the snapshot must be applied atomically. Mitigated by the fact that all call sites already tolerate `try?` best-effort semantics.

#### D02 — Browse is one non-materialized UNION view, fetched whole and sorted in RAM with no pagination

- **Severity:** Critical | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:8-40`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:33-40`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:88-95`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:131`
- **Problem:** Every browse, folder view, search-result hydration, dedupe scan, peek, and dedupe-key build runs `SELECT * FROM (<localSelect> UNION ALL <driveSelect>) ORDER BY takenAtMs DESC` with no LIMIT/OFFSET. The UNION is an inline derived table re-parsed and re-planned at each of ~12 call sites, and its top-level `ORDER BY takenAtMs DESC` cannot use the `idx assets.takenAtMs` index because the column emerges from a derived UNION — so SQLite materializes the full union into a temp b-tree and sorts it. `timelineItems` then returns ALL TimelineItem structs to the main actor (AppState.swift:131), where `groupedSections` walks the entire array. At 100k assets this is ~100k structs + a full temp-sort per browse; at 1M it is a multi-hundred-MB allocation and a guaranteed UI hitch on every Space switch / filter change. There is no pagination anywhere in the read path. This is the documented scaling ceiling and directly blocks the 'friend's real 10k import' acceptance test growing into the intended large-library and server-consumer roadmap.
- **Proposed change:** Promote the union to a first-class browseable projection rather than re-deriving it inline. Two complementary moves: (1) Make `timelineSQL` a real SQL VIEW (or a materialized `browse_rows` table refreshed on scan-reconcile) with a covering index on `(takenAtMs DESC, kind, isLivePairedVideo)` so the timeline order is index-served, not temp-sorted. (2) Add keyset pagination to the public API: `timelineItems(before: takenAtMs?, limit: Int)` returning a page, and have LibraryService/AppState page the grid (the grid already needs windowing for the Phase-5 tile renderer). Keep the in-RAM `[TimelineItem]` only for small result sets (search hits), not for whole-library browse.
- **Risk:** Medium-High. A materialized table adds a refresh path that must stay consistent with instances/vault_presence (mitigated because the catalog is declared rebuildable). A VIEW is lower-risk but doesn't fix the temp-sort unless paired with the covering index. Pagination touches AppState's grid model and FolderGridView — a moderate blast radius but mechanical. No on-disk format change (catalog is rebuildable), so no docs/format migration cost.

### High

#### D03 — Drives/role orchestration sprawl: ~10 methods hand-repeat the same presence→badge→drift→queries refresh sequence with no reconcile primitive

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** duplication | **Subsystem:** AppState architecture | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1109 (driftScan)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1128 (verifyAllConnected)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1188 (verifyIntegrity)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1209 (autoScanConnectedDrives)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:763-808 (recoverCanonical/cloneToBackup)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:972-988 (refreshCanonicalPresence/reloadCanonicalPresence)`
- **Problem:** The drives subsystem is ~640 lines inside AppState and the role/sync/drift methods repeat a near-identical fixed sequence: DriftReconciler.scan/verify → annotateRecoverability(presenceService) → catalog.replaceVaultPresence(presenceEntries(...)) → reloadCanonicalPresence() → driveDrift[id]=report → refreshPendingDeletions(). This appears verbatim across driftScan, verifyAllConnected, verifyIntegrity, autoScanConnectedDrives, and is partially repeated in cloneToBackup/recoverCanonical/promoteToCanonical (each ends with reloadDrives(); reloadCanonicalPresence(); try? refreshQueries()). The duplication means a change to the reconcile contract (e.g. presence semantics, the snapshot-write step) must be made in ~6 places and is easy to get subtly inconsistent — a correctness risk for the canonical/backup presence sets that drive sovereignty-critical badges and deletion eligibility. It also couples AppState directly to DriftReconciler/Manifest/SyncEngine/CatalogSnapshot internals.
- **Proposed change:** Extract a `DriveCoordinator` (Core or App-side @MainActor) owning durableVaults/canonicalPresence/driveDrift/drivePendingDeletions/ejectedDrives/driveKinds and exposing intent methods (scan/verify/repair/clone/recover/promote/forget). Factor the repeated tail into one private primitive, e.g. `applyDriftResult(_ report, for: drive)` that does annotate→replaceVaultPresence→reloadPresence→store→refreshPendingDeletions, and one `reconcileAfterRoleChange()` for the reloadDrives+presence+queries tail. AppState delegates Drives-view calls to this coordinator. Move the Manifest/SyncEngine touch-points behind a Core method so the App layer stops reaching into Core sync internals.
- **Risk:** Medium: the sequence ordering is load-bearing (driftScan re-derives presence BEFORE refreshQueries reads it — see evict at line 1608), so the extracted primitive must preserve ordering exactly. Pure mechanical extraction with no behavior change; well-covered by the existing drive tests if any, otherwise needs targeted tests around the reconcile primitive.

#### D04 — Single @Observable god object: seven cohesive subsystems share one invalidation surface and one 1740-line file

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** architecture | **Subsystem:** AppState architecture | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:51 (class AppState)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:164-528 (search state+runSearch)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:192-401 (people state+management)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:231-293 (cull state)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:662-1306 (drives/roles/drift ~640 lines)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1453-1529 (derivation runner)`
- **Problem:** AppState owns the state and orchestration for library/query, search, people, cull, drives/roles, derivation, send, peek, import, settings toggles, and undo — all as flat stored properties on one @Observable class bound into 34 views as `@Bindable var state` with 73 distinct member accesses. Consequences: (a) publishing granularity is all-or-nothing — mutating searchResults invalidates the Timeline, Folders, People and Drives views because they all observe the same object; (b) the file is unmaintainable and every feature widens the same surface; (c) there are no testable seams — testing search ranking or cull grouping requires instantiating the whole @MainActor god object with a live LibraryService; (d) the documented roadmap (people, cull, search refinement) keeps growing this class. The subsystems are already cleanly separable: search state is self-contained (searchQuery/searchFilters/searchResults/semanticIndex/runSearch), people likewise (people/suggestedClusters/loadPeople + the 6 management methods), cull likewise, derivation likewise.
- **Proposed change:** Decompose into focused `@Observable @MainActor` models owned by AppState (which becomes a thin coordinator holding navigation/selection + the shared library handle): SearchModel, PeopleModel, CullModel, DrivesModel (see next finding), DerivationRunner, and a BrowseModel (sections/flatItems/folderTree/binEntries). Each owns its state and its orchestration methods; each is injected into its view subtree via @Environment so a search mutation only invalidates Search views. Cross-model coordination (e.g. a move that must refresh browse + presence) goes through a small set of explicit calls or an event, not shared mutable fields. Move the nonisolated sidecar helpers into a Core `PersonSidecarWriter` (see error/concurrency finding).
- **Risk:** High blast radius but mechanical: 34 views change their binding from `state.x` to `searchModel.x`/`peopleModel.x` etc., and OpenPhotoApp.swift must construct + inject the sub-models. Low correctness risk because behavior is unchanged; can be done subsystem-by-subsystem (extract SearchModel first as a vertical slice, prove the pattern, then People/Cull) so it is incrementally shippable.

#### D05 — Folder browse/counts rely on GLOB recursion a B-tree cannot serve

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:61-136`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/Catalog+Search.swift:41-56`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:385-411`
- **Problem:** Recursive folder browse (`items(inDir:recursive:)`), the structured-filter folder facet, and `rewriteVaultPresencePaths` all match subtrees via `dirPath GLOB '<dir>/*'`. SQLite cannot use a b-tree index for a GLOB whose pattern doesn't reduce to a literal prefix range, so each recursive folder open is a full scan of the union (instances + vault_presence). `folderCounts` additionally GROUP BYs `dirPath` over both branches plus a correlated `MIN(rowid)` dedupe per drive-only row — full scan of vault_presence on every Folders-view render. The `dirPath` index that exists is only usable for the exact-match (non-recursive) case. This caps the Folders view, which is a primary navigation surface, and the rewrite-on-move path scales with total presence rows on every folder drag.
- **Proposed change:** Two options. Cheap: exploit that GLOB '<dir>/*' is a prefix range — rewrite as `dirPath >= '<dir>/' AND dirPath < '<dir>/￿'` (or the byte-successor of '/') so the existing `dirPath` b-tree serves it, keeping the Swift-side hasPrefix guard. Structural: add a `folder_depth`/materialized closure or store a normalized `pathSegments` and index a `(dirPrefix)` column, letting recursive counts be a single GROUP BY over an indexed range. Precompute `folderCounts` incrementally on scan-reconcile into a `folder_counts(dirPath, n)` cache table rather than recomputing the GROUP BY + correlated dedupe on every render.
- **Risk:** Medium. The range-rewrite is low-risk and local but must handle the collation/successor-character edge correctly (GLOB is case-sensitive, default collation is BINARY — they happen to align, but this needs a test). A folder_counts cache adds a refresh path. No format change.

#### D06 — SemanticIndex holds all embeddings in one fp32 RAM matrix with a full per-query sort

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/SemanticIndex.swift:6-39`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog+Embeddings.swift:47-55`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:487-519`
- **Problem:** `SemanticIndex.init` calls `allEmbeddings(model:)`, unpacking every stored Float16 vector to Float and concatenating into one contiguous `[Float]` of count×dim. For a typical CLIP dim of 512–768, fp32: at 100k assets that is 100k×768×4 ≈ 295 MB resident (≈590 MB at dim 768/100k if 1024-dim); at 1M assets ≈ 3 GB — on a Mac that already OOM'd to 41 GB during indexing (per project memory). The full index is rebuilt from scratch whenever `semanticIndexDirty` (AppState.swift:502-504), re-reading and re-unpacking the entire embeddings table on the search task. `query` then does a full vDSP_mmul over all rows and an O(N log N) `.sorted()` of the whole score array to take topN — no partial-select, no ANN. This is a brute-force design that is fine at a few thousand assets and unusable at the roadmap's target scale, and the full-rebuild-on-dirty pattern means every new embedding invalidates and re-materializes hundreds of MB.
- **Proposed change:** Decouple the index abstraction from the brute-force impl behind a `SemanticSearcher` protocol so the storage strategy can evolve without touching callers. Near-term: keep vectors as Float16 in RAM (halves footprint) and convert to fp32 only inside the vDSP call, and replace the full `.sorted()` with a bounded top-N selection (partial heap / `vDSP` + a k-selection) — O(N) instead of O(N log N). Medium-term: make the index incremental (append new rows instead of full rebuild on dirty) and add an on-disk ANN tier (e.g. an IVF/HNSW sidecar or sqlite-vec) so 1M vectors don't need to be resident. The protocol seam lets the brute-force path remain the small-library fallback.
- **Risk:** Medium. The Float16-resident + partial-select change is low-risk and local to SemanticIndex. Incremental updates require coordinating with AppState's dirty flag. An on-disk ANN tier is a larger dependency decision; gate it behind the protocol so it's additive. Embedding blob format is unchanged (already Float16 LE) so no format-doc change.

#### D07 — `assets` (the hot filter table) has only a takenAtMs index; structured filters full-scan

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Catalog, queries & search | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:39-56`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Search/Catalog+Search.swift:10-107`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog+Derivation.swift:23-38`
- **Problem:** The `assets` table is indexed only on `takenAtMs` (plus the `hash` PK). But `structuredFilter` predicates on `kind`, `favorite`, `rating`, `cameraModel`, `livePairHash` and every query filters `isLivePairedVideo = 0`; `distinctCameras` scans `cameraModel`; `pendingDerivation`/`derivationProgress` filter `kind = ? AND isLivePairedVideo = 0` (+ `latitude/longitude` for geocode); `geotaggedAssets` filters `latitude IS NOT NULL`. None of these columns are indexed, so each is a full scan of `assets` — and inside the timeline union, which is itself a temp-materialized full scan. As the library grows, every facet click, every derivation-runner poll (`pendingDerivation` runs repeatedly with a LEFT JOIN on derivation_jobs), and every map open re-scans the whole table. The index coverage simply does not match the documented query surface.
- **Proposed change:** Add targeted secondary indexes matched to the actual predicates: a partial index `CREATE INDEX idx_assets_browse ON assets(takenAtMs DESC) WHERE isLivePairedVideo = 0` (serves the dominant browse + hides paired videos for free), `idx_assets_kind(kind) WHERE isLivePairedVideo = 0`, `idx_assets_camera(cameraModel)`, and a partial geo index `idx_assets_geo(takenAtMs) WHERE latitude IS NOT NULL`. For favorites/rating, a partial `idx_assets_fav(takenAtMs) WHERE favorite = 1`. Add these in a single new migration (v13) — pure index DDL on a rebuildable table, no schema/format change.
- **Risk:** Low. Index-only additive migration; bump schemaVersion to 13 and add a changelog line in docs/format/catalog-schema.md per the documentation-discipline rule. Slightly larger catalog file and marginally slower writes during bulk scan ingest (acceptable; ingest is batched in one transaction).

#### D08 — All matchers are brute-force O(n²) with no spatial/ANN index — blocks the 10k+ library roadmap

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** Cull & faces (clustering/dedup) | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:43-53`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Cull/DuplicateGrouper.swift:18-23`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Cull/BurstGrouper.swift:13-22`
- **Problem:** Every similarity matcher does full pairwise comparison. FaceClusterer is O(n·k) clusters but each membership test scans ALL members (single-link), degenerating to O(n²) cosine over 512-dim Float when faces collapse into few large clusters — exactly the chaining case. DuplicateGrouper is O(m²) Hamming within each folder bucket (DuplicateGrouper.swift:18-23); one big folder (a 5k-photo dump) is 12.5M comparisons. BurstGrouper is linear (only adjacent pairs) so it is fine. There is zero ANN/LSH/sort-prune infrastructure anywhere in Sources (grep confirms). loadCullGroups/loadPeople load the ENTIRE embeddings/phash table into memory and run this single-threaded inside one Task.detached — for the documented 10k import this is the same memory-pressure/CPU-hog class of problem already flagged for indexing. This is the explicit roadmap blocker (friend's real ~10k import is the acceptance test).
- **Proposed change:** Introduce a thin nearest-neighbour layer rather than scattering loops. For dHash dedup: BK-tree or multi-band LSH on the 64-bit hash to prune candidates before Hamming (turns O(m²) into ~O(m log m)). For faces: blocking/canopy via LSH buckets on the embedding before exact cosine, so clustering only compares within candidate buckets. Encapsulate as a `NearestNeighborIndex` protocol in Core with a trivial brute-force impl (current behavior) and an LSH/BK-tree impl, selected by N. Stream from the catalog in chunks instead of materializing the whole table. Keep the pure grouper signatures; they consume candidate pairs from the index.
- **Risk:** Medium-High. New abstraction and the most algorithmically involved change, but it sits behind the existing pure-function boundary so callers (AppState) and the on-disk format are untouched. Main risk is recall regressions from approximate pruning — mitigate by keeping brute-force as the default below a size threshold and as the test oracle.

#### D09 — Face identity clustered on a generic scene feature-print, and named people are ignored during clustering

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** abstraction | **Subsystem:** Cull & faces (clustering/dedup) | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/FaceStage.swift:49-71`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog+Faces.swift:112-123`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:208-228`
- **Problem:** FaceStage runs VNGenerateImageFeaturePrint on a padded face CROP (FaceStage.swift:49,56-71). VNGenerateImageFeaturePrint is a general-purpose image similarity descriptor, NOT a face-identity embedding (it is not trained to be invariant to pose/lighting/expression for the same identity, and not discriminative across identities). The clustering quality ceiling is therefore set by the wrong embedding, independent of the linkage fix. Separately, the clustering pipeline only ever consumes unassignedFacesWithEmbeddings() (personID IS NULL AND source='auto') — it NEVER compares an unassigned face against existing named people's confirmed faces (Catalog+Faces.swift:112-123, AppState.swift:216-217). So once you name 'Alice', new photos of Alice are clustered only among themselves and re-suggested as an unknown blob, instead of being proposed as 'likely Alice'. The abstraction conflates 'visual look-alike grouping' with 'identity recognition' and only implements the former.
- **Proposed change:** Two-part. (1) Treat the embedding source as a named, versioned policy: add a face-embedding model identifier alongside the vector (mirror the embeddings table's `model` column, which faces lacks) so a future real face-recognition model can supersede VNGenerateImageFeaturePrint via the same reconcile/re-derive path. (2) Add a recognition step distinct from cold-start clustering: a `assignToNearestPerson(face, people, threshold)` that compares each unassigned face to per-person centroids of confirmed faces, surfacing 'add to <Person>?' suggestions; reserve agglomerative clustering for the genuinely-unknown remainder. This splits the conflated abstraction into 'cluster unknowns' vs 'recognize against known'.
- **Risk:** Medium. The recognition step is additive and self-contained (new query + new pure function), low blast radius. Swapping the embedding model is the bigger move: it forces a re-derivation of all faces and a format-doc update (per CLAUDE.md, the faces embedding is machine-derived and rebuildable, so no user-data risk, but the catalog-schema doc must record the model column).

#### D10 — FaceClusterer uses greedy single-link agglomeration → transitive chaining merges distinct people

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Cull & faces (clustering/dedup) | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:43-60`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:217`
- **Problem:** cluster() joins an item to the FIRST existing cluster where ANY member is within threshold (single-link, FaceClusterer.swift:47-49). Single-link clustering is the textbook 'chaining' failure mode: if A~B and B~C but A is far from C, A, B, C all collapse into one cluster. With faces of the same gender/lighting/pose this transitively bridges different people into one giant blob, while a tight threshold over-fragments the same person across pose changes. There is no centroid, no average/complete linkage, and no notion of cluster cohesion. Order-dependence compounds it: the FIRST matching cluster wins and clusters never split or re-merge, so result quality depends on input row order. This is a correctness defect in the headline user-facing feature (People suggestions), and it caps cluster quality regardless of how the 0.4 threshold is tuned.
- **Proposed change:** Replace greedy single-link with a centroid-based or density-based scheme. Minimal: maintain a running unit-mean centroid per cluster and assign each face to the nearest centroid within threshold (k-means-like / online centroid linkage) — kills chaining, still O(n·k). Better target: factor a small `Clustering` abstraction with a pluggable `Linkage`/`ClusterModel` strategy (centroid now, HDBSCAN/DBSCAN later) so the algorithm is swappable behind FaceClusterer.cluster's stable signature. Keep the deterministic largest-first ordering. Add adversarial chaining tests (A~B~C with A far from C must NOT co-cluster).
- **Risk:** Medium. Signature (items, threshold)->[[Int64]] is unchanged and only AppState.loadPeople and tests call it, so blast radius is contained. Risk is behavioral: thresholds tuned for single-link won't transfer to centroid linkage, so the 0.4 default must be re-tuned and snapshot tests updated. No persisted data migrates (clusters are recomputed each load).

#### D11 — Derivation runner is embedded in the @MainActor AppState god object instead of Core

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** architecture | **Subsystem:** Derivation / ML pipeline | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1453`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1461`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1473`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1520`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift`
- **Problem:** The pipeline orchestration policy — stage registry, poke/idempotency guard, the whole drain loop, the goodCopyURL/needsFile reachability rules, progress aggregation, and the post-drain dirty-flag fanout (semanticIndexDirty/facesDirty/geocodeDirty) — lives entirely in AppState (drainDerivation/pokeDerivation/combinedProgress, AppState.swift:1453-1529), the ~1740-line @MainActor UI god object. The derivation domain logic is thus coupled to SwiftUI/@Observable: it cannot be unit-tested without AppState, cannot be driven headless (CLI re-index, server canonical-drive consumer per CLAUDE.md sovereignty roadmap), and the Core façade (LibraryService) owns none of it despite owning catalog/scan/import. Each `run` is wrapped in its own `Task.detached(.utility)` (AppState.swift:1498) one asset at a time, so the orchestration and the off-main hop are interleaved in the view layer rather than expressed as a reusable Core service.
- **Proposed change:** Extract a `DerivationRunner` (plain Sendable actor/struct) into OpenPhotoCore that owns the stage registry, the drain loop, reachability policy, and retry/skip rules, exposing e.g. `func drain(resolveURL: (String) -> URL?, progress: (StageProgress) -> Void) async` and `func remainingWork() -> (done,total)`. AppState keeps only: the poke trigger, the resolveURL closure (Mac-local/connected-drive lookup), and publishing progress + setting the dirty flags. This makes the pipeline headless-testable and reusable by a future CLI/server, and shrinks AppState. The DerivationStage protocol and the stages move/stay in Core unchanged.
- **Risk:** Medium. Pure code-movement with a small seam (URL-resolution + progress callbacks) crossing the App→Core boundary; no format/schema change. Blast radius limited to AppState and a new Core type; existing stage unit tests unaffected. Must preserve the whole-pending-set drain semantics (the starvation fix) exactly.

#### D12 — EmbedStage model + tokenizer rebuilt per search query (no shared, owned model lifetime)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** Derivation / ML pipeline | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:510`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1456`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:44`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:67`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:95`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/EmbedStage.swift:104`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Derivation/CLIPTokenizer.swift:29`
- **Problem:** EmbedStage's lazy/memoized load state (imageModel/textModel/tokenizer + tried* flags, EmbedStage.swift:34-39) is per-instance, but the search path constructs a brand-new instance every time: `EmbedStage().embedText(q)` (AppState.swift:510). runSearch() fires on a 300ms keystroke debounce (Search/SearchView.swift:164-166), so each search builds a fresh EmbedStage whose triedTextLoad/triedTokenizerLoad are false → it runs MLModel.compileModel + MLModel(contentsOf:) for the text encoder AND rebuilds the entire CLIP BPE tokenizer (gunzip of bpe_simple_vocab_16e6.txt.gz, ~49k-entry encoder dict, 48,895-entry merge-rank dict, regex compile — CLIPTokenizer.init, CLIPTokenizer.swift:29-93) on the query hot path. Furthermore the registry's EmbedStage (AppState.swift:1456) is a different instance from the search instances, so the image+text models are compiled at least twice and never shared. The lock/memoization machinery (EmbedStage.swift:30,86-113) is effectively dead for the query path because the instance never survives a second call. Consequence: large, repeated latency and CPU/ANE compile churn on every search keystroke-batch; the in-built caching is structurally defeated.
- **Proposed change:** Give the compiled models and tokenizer a single owned lifetime. Concretely: introduce one long-lived `EmbedStage` (or an `EmbeddingModel` actor wrapping it) created once when the library opens, stored on AppState (or better, behind LibraryService as `lib.embedder`), and inject that same instance both into the derivationStages registry and into runSearch (replace `EmbedStage().embedText(q)` and `EmbedStage().modelID` with the shared instance). Optionally split EmbedStage into an `EmbeddingModel` (owns MLModel + tokenizer, thread-safe via an actor or the existing NSLock) and a thin `EmbedDerivationStage` adapter, mirroring the OCR/Face split, so the model lifetime is explicit and not tied to a DerivationStage value. The `.modelID` reads at AppState.swift:254/503/1350 are cheap (string only) and can stay or also use the shared instance for consistency.
- **Risk:** Low–Medium. Localized to AppState wiring + EmbedStage ownership; no on-disk format or catalog-schema change, so no third-party/doc impact. Main care: ensure thread-safety for concurrent runner-vs-query access (NSLock already present) and invalidate/reuse correctly across library switches.

#### D13 — ImportRegistry rewrites its entire backing file on every appended row (O(N²) per import session)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Import engines | **Effort:** S
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportRegistry.swift:78`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportRegistry.swift:83`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportEngine.swift:97`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportEngine.swift:149`
- **Problem:** `imports.jsonl` is named and documented as an append log, but `append(_:)` re-encodes the ENTIRE in-memory `byKey` map, sorts it, and atomically rewrites the whole file for each single entry (lines 83-89). The engine calls `append` once per item — once per skipped duplicate in the fetch loop (ImportEngine.swift:97) and once per verified import in the verify loop (line 149). So importing N items rewrites the file N times, each rewrite serializing the full cumulative history: total work is O(N²) bytes written, with an fsync per item. On the documented 10k-item real-world import this is ~10k full-file fsync rewrites of an ever-growing file — minutes of pointless I/O and write amplification, and it scales worse as the registry accumulates across the device's lifetime.
- **Proposed change:** Make the log actually append-only: keep the in-memory `byKey`/`byHash` indexes, but on `append` write only the single new line via an O(1) durable append (open-for-append + fsync, or buffer the batch and flush once). Expose a batch API `append(_ entries: [Entry])` that the engine calls once after the fetch loop and once after the verify loop, so a batch is at most two writes. Compaction (the only place a full rewrite is justified — to drop superseded keys) becomes an explicit infrequent operation, not a side effect of every insert. Since each line is already self-contained JSON and load() already tolerates arbitrary line order, appended-only files remain readable with no format change.
- **Risk:** Low–moderate: ImportRegistry is consumed read-only elsewhere (PresenceService, BackupProbe, FreeUpPhoneView) via the in-memory indexes, which are unaffected. Must keep crash-atomicity per line (append+fsync is atomic enough for a log); document the append semantics in vault-format-v1 §12, which is a required doc touch under the project's format-discipline rule.

#### D14 — ImportSource protocol underspecifies real capabilities; engine and UI downcast to concrete source types

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** abstraction | **Subsystem:** Import engines | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ImportSource.swift:43`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/Devices/ImportView.swift:400`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/Devices/ImportView.swift:401`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/Devices/ImportView.swift:404`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/Devices/ImportView.swift:408`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/VolumeSource.swift:14`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/VolumeSource.swift:112`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ForeignVaultSource.swift:41`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Import/ForeignVaultSource.swift:77`
- **Problem:** The `ImportSource` protocol models a generic fetch/enumerate/delete device, but the real per-source behaviors that the engine and UI depend on live OFF the protocol as concrete-type members: VolumeSource.foldXMPSidecars / enumerationProgress / sawXMPSidecars, ForeignVaultSource.sidecarData / folderCounts / knownHash semantics, TakeoutSource.looksLikeTakeout (static). To drive them, `ImportView.runBatch` does `source as? VolumeSource`, `source as? ForeignVaultSource` and then reaches in to set mutable flags and build out-of-band `subdirForItem` / `postPlace` closures that the engine takes as opaque parameters (ImportView.swift:400-416). The engine is thus only superficially source-agnostic: the knowledge of 'foreign vaults preserve their tree and carry sidecars' is encoded in the UI, not in the source. Consequence: adding the next source (the roadmap explicitly anticipates more import origins) requires touching the UI's downcast ladder and the engine's parameter surface, not just writing one adapter; the metadata-carry path is split between VolumeSource.fetch (inline XMP fold) and ForeignVaultSource (postPlace closure in the UI), so 'carry their metadata' means two different things in two places.
- **Proposed change:** Push capability into the protocol as small, defaulted, source-owned hooks rather than UI downcasts. (a) Add `func destinationSubpath(for: ImportItem) -> String` (default "") so foreign-vault tree-preservation is the source's own knowledge, not a UI closure. (b) Replace the VolumeSource mutable `foldXMPSidecars` flag and the ForeignVaultSource `sidecarData`+postPlace pair with one protocol method, e.g. `func carriedSidecar(for: ImportItem) -> SidecarData?` (default nil), and have the engine apply it uniformly between place and rescan — collapsing the two metadata-carry implementations into one. (c) Move `enumerationProgress` into the `enumerateItems` signature (pass a progress callback) instead of a pre-set property. (d) Add an `ImportCapabilities` option set (deletable, hasReclaimableTrash, offersMetadataCarry) the UI reads, eliminating `as?` for feature gating. The engine then needs no concrete-type knowledge.
- **Risk:** Moderate blast radius: touches all five sources, the engine signature, and ImportView. Mechanical and well-contained (one subsystem), with existing unit tests on FakeSource to anchor it; no on-disk format change.

#### D15 — Move/folder-reorg use case is split across the Core↔App boundary; multi-drive format logic lives in SwiftUI

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** coupling | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService+Move.swift:18`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:109`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:128-209`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState+FolderReorg.swift:260-290`
- **Problem:** Core's `movePhotos` is only half of the move operation: it moves files in the local primary vault and returns a `MoveResult`. Everything that makes a move correct under OpenPhoto's invariants — propagating the move to every connected durable drive, queueing `moveFile` folder-ops for offline drives, re-keying drive-only presence rows (`rewriteVaultPresencePath`), mapping mac-relative paths to drive-prefixed paths (`mapToDriveStatic`), and assembling the `MovedFileRecord` undo log — lives in `AppState+FolderReorg.movePhotos(ids:into:)` (≈100 lines) and the sibling `createFolder`/`deleteFolder` methods. This is format-level orchestration (the same one-way-sync, basename-aligned, queue-when-offline rules the format docs are normative about) sitting in the SwiftUI/@MainActor layer. Consequence: the canonical-drive write path cannot be exercised without the app, the documented invariants are enforced in a UI file rather than Core, the same drive-propagate/queue boilerplate is copy-pasted across move/create/delete folder ops, and a future headless/server consumer of the canonical drive has no Core API to reuse.
- **Proposed change:** Introduce a Core-level orchestrator (e.g. `VaultReorgService` or methods on `LibraryService`) that owns the full transaction: `func moveAssets(_ items:[TimelineItem], toDir:String, connectedDrives:[Vault], offlineDriveIDs:[String]) throws -> ReorgResult`, where ReorgResult carries both the local `MoveResult` and the `[MovedFileRecord]` undo log. Move `mapToDrive`/basename mapping, presence re-keying, and folder-op enqueue into Core. AppState shrinks to: gather connected/offline drives, call the Core op off-main, then rescan/refresh/recordUndo. Do the same for create/delete folder so the three share one propagation primitive.
- **Risk:** Medium-high blast radius: touches the most-used mutation path and the offline-queue format contract. Mitigate by keeping `movePhotos` as-is and adding the orchestrator alongside, migrating call sites one at a time; the existing VaultReorganizer/catalog ops are reused unchanged, so behavior can be held identical and covered by Core tests before deleting the AppState logic.

#### D16 — Synchronous façade I/O on the main actor; folderTree does an unbounded FS walk during refresh

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** LibraryService orchestration & selection | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:178`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:150`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1531-1546`
- **Problem:** `AppState.refreshQueries()` runs on `@MainActor` and calls `timelineSections`, `folderTree`, and `binItems` synchronously. `timelineItems` materializes the entire library (the local∪drive UNION, ordered) into an array on the main thread; `folderTree` additionally calls `directoriesUnder(primaryRoot)` — a full recursive `FileManager.enumerator` walk of the vault root with per-URL resourceValues/symlink resolution — unioned with the `folderCounts` SQL aggregate, all on the main thread. refreshQueries runs after every delete/move/rename/restore/evict/rehydrate, so the cost is paid on every mutation and scales with library + folder count, risking visible main-thread stalls on large libraries (consistent with the recorded dense-grid/Space-switch hitch). Because `LibraryService` is a plain `Sendable` class wrapping a thread-safe GRDB `DatabaseQueue`, nothing structurally forces this work off-main — the type's design invites main-thread calls.
- **Proposed change:** Keep `LibraryService` a Sendable class (an actor would needlessly serialize the already-thread-safe GRDB queue and force await on cheap calls), but make the browse surface explicitly background: have `refreshQueries` build sections/folderTree/binItems inside `Task.detached(.utility)` and publish the results back via `MainActor.run`, matching the pattern already used everywhere else in AppState. Separately, split `folderTree` into a cheap `folderCounts`-only tree and an opt-in/cached FS-walk pass (the empty-dir union rarely changes); cache `directoriesUnder` and invalidate only on folder create/delete rather than re-walking on every photo mutation.
- **Risk:** Low-to-medium: changing refreshQueries to async-publish can introduce transient stale UI between mutation and refresh, but that window already exists. The folderTree split is internal to Core with no format impact. Main risk is ordering/races around the `refreshToken`/`expandedFolders` seeding logic, which must move into the main-actor publish step.

#### D17 — No orphan-asset pruning: assets/presence rows for vanished content are never removed

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:127-143`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:470-475`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Queries.swift:28-30`
- **Problem:** scan reconciles instances via `replaceInstances` (DELETE all rows for the vault, re-insert current ones), so per-vault instance rows are correct. But `assets` rows are only ever inserted (`catalog.upsert(assets:)`), never deleted — there is no DELETE FROM assets anywhere in the codebase. When a file is deleted outside the bin flow (or moved off the canonical drive), its `assets` row, and any drive-only `vault_presence` row, persists forever. Because the browse path is a UNION of local instances and drive-only presence rows (timelineSQL), a hash with no remaining instance but a lingering presence/asset row can still surface as a ghost timeline entry, and `knownHashes` keeps returning it so it's never re-extracted. For a rebuildable catalog whose whole premise is 'derivable from the files', unbounded monotonic growth with no GC is a real data-model correctness gap — and a third-party/server consumer reading the canonical drive's catalog would inherit the ghosts.
- **Proposed change:** Add a reconciliation step at end of scan (or a periodic catalog GC): after writing instances for all local vaults, delete `assets` rows whose hash has no instance in any local vault AND no presence row in any registered drive vault (i.e. truly unreferenced). Encapsulate as `catalog.pruneOrphanAssets()` run once after a full `scanAll`, not per-vault (a hash may live only in vault B while vault A is scanned first). Document the GC rule in catalog-schema docs since it defines catalog lifecycle for external readers.
- **Risk:** Medium. Deleting asset rows must not race with derivation stages or drop human-metadata that should have been moved to a sidecar; pruning must run after all vaults are reconciled, not inside per-vault scan, or it will delete cross-vault-only assets. Needs the 'last full scan' notion. Touches catalog write surface + browse correctness.

#### D18 — Scan is strictly single-threaded; the parallelizable hashing+extraction never uses Task.detached parallelism

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:63-85`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:91-122`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/LibraryService.swift:56-65`
- **Problem:** Hashing (`ContentHash.ofFile`, the O(bytes) cost) and metadata extraction (`MetadataExtractor.extract`, which already `await`s AVFoundation for video) run in a plain serial `for` loop. The whole scan is offloaded once via `Task.detached(.utility)` in LibraryService, but inside the scan there is zero concurrency — on a multi-core Mac indexing tens of thousands of files, the dominant I/O+CPU work runs on one core. The design explicitly intends heavy work to run via `Task.detached(.utility)`, and the memory note flags 'single-threaded indexing still needs bounded-parallel work'. The monolithic structure (finding 1) is what blocks this: because all stages are fused in one function over shared mutable arrays, you can't drop in a bounded `TaskGroup` without first separating the stages.
- **Proposed change:** After the streaming refactor, run the hashing and extraction stages through a bounded `withTaskGroup` (concurrency capped to ~ActiveProcessorCount, with backpressure so only N files are in flight — preserving the per-file autoreleasepool memory bound). Keep catalog writes serialized (GRDB dbQueue is already serial) by funneling results back through an actor or a serial collector. Order-independence already holds: pairing and persistence operate on the full set, not on walk order.
- **Risk:** Medium. Concurrency bugs are easy to introduce; needs careful backpressure so parallel hashing doesn't reintroduce the OOM. Must confirm ImageIO/AVFoundation calls are safe off the main actor (they are). Depends on finding 1 landing first. Blast radius limited to Scanner internals.

#### D19 — scan is a monolithic, fully-materialized, non-resumable pass — O(files)+O(manifest) RAM

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** architecture | **Subsystem:** Scan & indexing pipeline | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:17-148`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:24`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:59-61`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Scanner/Scanner.swift:88-89`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/Manifest.swift:50-63`
- **Problem:** The whole pipeline is one ~130-line function that materializes every intermediate collection in memory before doing the next stage: `found` (every media file's rel/url/size/mtime/kind), `oldByPath` (the entire manifest as a Dictionary, O(M)), `aligned` (every file again, paired with its ManifestEntry), `known` (the full set of catalog hashes via SELECT hash FROM assets), `newAssets`, `pairCandidates`, and finally `instances`. For a large library these are 4-6 simultaneous arrays/sets of size O(files). Nothing streams, and there is no checkpointing: a crash or quit mid-scan discards all hashing work because the manifest and instances are only written in step 5 at the very end. This is the structural root of the open memory-safety roadmap item (#17 / the OOM memory note) — the leaf autoreleasepool fixes bounded per-file cost, but the per-library collections are still all-resident. It also blocks resumability and makes incremental scans pay full manifest-load cost every FSEvent.
- **Proposed change:** Split scan into a staged, streaming pipeline behind a small ScanPlanner/ScanRunner type. Stream the enumerator → fast-path decision → hashing → extraction as an AsyncSequence (or chunked batches of N files) rather than building `found`/`aligned`/`newAssets` in full. Replace the in-RAM `oldByPath` manifest dict with a keyed lookup: either load manifest rows into a temp SQLite/index keyed by path, or (better) make the catalog `instances` table the source of truth for the fast-path (it already holds path+size+mtime per vault) and drop the manifest-as-dict read entirely. Persist instances + manifest in batches/checkpoints so a mid-scan crash resumes instead of restarting. Emit `AssetRecord`/`InstanceRecord` per batch to `catalog.upsert`.
- **Risk:** Medium-High. Touches the core indexing logic and the manifest/catalog write ordering; must preserve the atomic-manifest invariant and the 'setLivePair for all pairs' healing behavior. Batched writes change failure semantics (partial progress becomes visible), so the format/recovery docs must be updated. Blast radius is contained to Scanner + Catalog write methods; callers (LibraryService.scanAll/rescan) keep the same signature.

#### D20 — Quadratic bulk repair/adopt/restore: per-file full manifest + full presence-table rewrite

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** concurrency-architecture | **Subsystem:** Sync & send engines | **Effort:** M
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:172 (writeManifestEntry: read-all + rewrite-all)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:93 (restore), :106 (repairCorrupt), :84 (adopt)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoApp/AppState.swift:1183 (repairAllRecoverable loop), :1256 (adoptAll loop), :1273 (restoreAllRecoverable loop)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/CatalogIngest.swift:33 (per-file vaultPresenceRows read-all + replaceVaultPresence DELETE-all/reinsert)`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Catalog/Catalog.swift:264 (replaceVaultPresence)`
- **Problem:** DriftReconciler.writeManifestEntry reads the ENTIRE manifest, removes one path, appends one, and rewrites the whole file (atomic temp→rename) on EVERY call. restore/repairCorrupt/adopt each call it once per file. The App's bulk operations (repairAllRecoverable, restoreAllRecoverable, adoptAll) loop over findings calling these one-at-a-time, so repairing/restoring/adopting K files re-reads and re-serializes the full N-line manifest K times: O(K·N) bytes rewritten and O(K) fsyncs. For a 10k-asset drive recovering 2k missing files that is ~20M manifest-line serializations and 2k full-file fsync-renames. CatalogIngest.ingestDriveFile compounds this: it fetches ALL presence rows for the vault and does a DELETE-all+reinsert replaceVaultPresence per file, so adoptAll is additionally O(K·P) on the SQLite presence table. moveToBin (called per file by repairCorrupt and DeletionPropagator) has the same read-all/rewrite-all shape on bin.jsonl. This directly threatens the documented 'friend's real 10k import is the acceptance test' roadmap milestone and the multi-thousand-file drive-recovery flows.
- **Proposed change:** Introduce batch repair APIs on DriftReconciler: repairAll(findings:from:)/adoptAll(relPaths:)/restoreAll(findings:) that (a) read the manifest ONCE into a [path: ManifestEntry] dict, (b) move/copy/hash each file, mutating the dict in memory, (c) do ONE Manifest.write at the end — mirroring the single-rewrite pattern DeletionPropagator.propagate already gets right. Similarly add Catalog.upsertVaultPresence(vaultID:entries:) (INSERT OR REPLACE the touched rows in one write) and a BinStore.moveBatch that appends bin entries once. Push the App's per-file loops down into these Core batch methods so AppState just calls one method.
- **Risk:** Medium. New batch methods are additive; the per-file methods can remain for single-file UI actions. The interruption-recovery story must be preserved (files still move before the single manifest write, so a crash mid-batch still self-heals as recoverable drift on the next scan) — this is the main correctness review point. Catalog upsert change is local to one file.

#### D21 — manifest.jsonl is a whole-file value with no index and no owner — per-file mutations are O(M), looped mutations O(M^2)

- **Severity:** High | **Confidence:** Confirmed | **Area:** data-model | **Subsystem:** Vault format, IO, sidecars | **Effort:** L
- **Location:** `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/Manifest.swift:38`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/Manifest.swift:50`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Vault/VaultReorganizer.swift:96`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:172`, `Sources/OpenPhotoCore/Sync/DeletionPropagator.swift:75`
- **Problem:** Manifest exposes only read([entries]) and write([entries]) over the entire file. Every mutation — moving one file (VaultReorganizer.rewriteManifestEntry:96), adopting/repairing one drive file (DriftReconciler.writeManifestEntry:172), acknowledging one gone file (acknowledgeGone:127) — reads all M lines, decodes M JSON objects, mutates one, re-sorts M, re-encodes M, and atomically rewrites the whole file. That is O(M) wall-clock and allocation per single-entry change. Worse, the only mutation primitive is whole-file, so any caller that needs N per-file edits is forced into N full read+write cycles = O(N*M); LibraryService+Move and AppState+FolderReorg already call VaultReorganizer.moveFile in loops, and DriftReconciler.adopt is called once per unknown file. There is also no owner: 10+ call sites across Scanner, Sync, Interop, App, and VaultReorganizer call Manifest.read/write on a bare URL, so invariants (sorted-by-path, NFC paths, atomicity) live by convention in each caller rather than behind a type.
- **Proposed change:** Introduce a ManifestStore(vault) façade that owns the file and an in-memory index (path -> ManifestEntry dictionary, like ImportRegistry already does for imports.jsonl). Expose entry(forPath:), upsert(_:), remove(path:), rename(from:to:), renameSubtree(oldDir:newDir:) and a single flush()/atomic write that batches a mutation set. Per-edit cost drops to O(1) in memory; batched edits flush once. Route VaultReorganizer, DriftReconciler, DeletionPropagator, SyncEngine, Scanner through it. Keep the JSONL on-disk shape identical (format unchanged) — this is purely an in-memory data-structure + ownership refactor.
- **Risk:** Medium. Broad call-site migration (10+ sites) but the on-disk format and tests of the format are untouched; can be landed incrementally by first adding the store and forwarding the existing free functions to it, then migrating hot loops (VaultReorganizer, Drift) first. Main correctness watch-item is concurrency: the store must be the single writer per vault or keep the current atomic-rewrite-per-flush semantics.

### Medium

- **D22 — Derivation runner is a private method-bag on AppState with no isolation seam, no per-stage observability, and ad-hoc dirty-flag fan-out** (`AppState.swift:1453-1467 (derivationTask/pokeDerivation)`, abstraction/M). The background derivation runner (the documented drain design) is implemented as private methods + a private Task handle on AppState, with its completion signalled by mutating three sibling dirty flags (semanticIndexDirty/facesDirty/geocodeDirty) that other subsystems (search/people/inspector) read. This couples the runner to search and people state, makes the runner untestable in isolation (it’s a private method on a @MainActor god object), and gives no structured progress beyond a single summed (done,total). The drain serially awaits each item via its own Task.detached — single-threaded inference — which the project memory flags as residual memory-safety/throughput work; there is no seam to bound parallelism. The cancel-on-close path (derivationTask?.cancel() at line 1394) is correct but the runner’s lifecycle is entangled with closeLibrary’s manual reset block. *Change:* Extract a `DerivationRunner` actor (or @MainActor coordinator wrapping a detached drain) owning derivationTask, the stage registry, and progress. Replace the three boolean dirty flags with an explicit completion signal — an AsyncStream/event `DerivationDidAdvance(stages:)` that SearchModel/PeopleModel subscribe to and mark THEIR OWN index dirty — so the runner no longer reaches into search/people state. This also isolates the place to add bounded parallelism (a TaskGroup with a width cap) addressing the documented residual.
- **D23 — People sidecar writes use nonisolated private methods on a @MainActor class — a misplaced Core responsibility and a concurrency-safety smell** (`AppState.swift:403-474 (nonisolated sidecar helpers)`, coupling/S). Three `nonisolated private` methods (writeSidecarRegions/clearSidecarRegion/rewriteSidecarForHash) perform real on-disk XMP sidecar writes (a sovereignty-critical, hard-invariant-bearing operation: human metadata → XMP) and live on the @MainActor UI god object, invoked as `self?.writeSidecarRegions(...)` from inside Task.detached blocks. This is a layering inversion — canonical-format writes belong in Core (SidecarStore is Core), not in the App view model — and the nonisolated-on-@MainActor pattern is a deliberate escape hatch that future Swift-6 isolation tightening or a refactor can silently break (a stray main-actor access inside these methods would not be caught). It also means the People management methods each re-derive person names and confirmed-face sets via repeated catalog.people() calls (line 416, 459) inside loops — O(persons) per face — entangling format-write logic with UI orchestration. *Change:* Move the three helpers into a Core `PersonSidecarWriter` (Sendable, takes LibraryService/Catalog + SidecarStore) with one public `rewriteSidecars(forPersonIDs:)` / `rewrite(forHashes:)` entry. The People management methods (which should live on a PeopleModel per finding 2) call it from their detached blocks. Cache the person-name lookup once per call instead of per-face. This restores the layering (format writes in Core), removes the nonisolated-on-MainActor hazard, and makes the sidecar logic unit-testable against a temp vault.
- **D24 — Whole-table Set builders (knownSizeDateKeys/assetHashes/knownHashes) over the union are an O(N) RAM tax on hot import/scan paths** (`Queries.swift:46-55`, api-design/M). `knownSizeDateKeys` runs the full timeline union just to project `(size, takenAtMs)` and build a String Set of `"size|second"` keys in RAM; `assetHashes`/`knownHashes` build a whole-table Set<String> of every hash; `instanceHashes` does `SELECT DISTINCT hash`. These are used on the import-flagging path (ImportView builds an in-memory presence cache before copies) and on every scanner reconcile (Scanner.swift:88). The pattern moves the entire keyspace into Swift Sets to answer membership questions the DB could answer with an indexed lookup. At 1M assets, `knownSizeDateKeys` alone allocates ~1M short strings; running the full union (with its temp-sort cost) purely to build a fingerprint set is wasteful. The deeper issue is an API-design one: membership/probe questions are modeled as 'hand me the whole set' rather than 'does X exist'. *Change:* Replace bulk-Set returns with probe APIs where the caller does point lookups: `containsSizeDateKey(size:second:)` backed by an index on `(size, takenAtMs)`, and `containsHash(_:)` backed by the PK. Where the caller genuinely needs the whole set (e.g. a one-shot foreign-import diff), keep a streaming/batched accessor instead of materializing in one allocation. For `knownSizeDateKeys` specifically, query `instances` + `vault_presence` directly rather than the full ORDER-BY-less union (the union's sort isn't needed for a Set).
- **D25 — instanceID-as-string ('vaultID|relPath') is the grid identity but has no supporting index** (`Records.swift:111-113`, abstraction/M). The grid's stable identity is the synthesized string `vaultID + '|' + relPath`, and `items(instanceIDs:)` resolves a selection back to rows with `WHERE vaultID || '|' || relPath IN (...)` over the full union. The concatenated expression cannot use the `(vaultID, relPath)` primary key, so every multi-select resolution is a full union scan + per-row string concat + IN-list match. The identity is encoded structurally (string concat parsed and re-split at boundaries) rather than as a typed value, which also leaks the delimiter convention across modules (selection, drag, FolderReorg). This is a coupling/abstraction smell plus an index-coverage miss on the select-and-move path, which the roadmap just shipped. *Change:* Introduce a small `InstanceID { vaultID; relPath }` value type (Codable, with a single canonical string encoding used only at UI/drag boundaries) and resolve selections by passing the components, querying `WHERE (vaultID, relPath) IN (VALUES ...)` or a temp-table join so the PK is used. Drive-only rows (no instances PK) resolve via `(vaultID, relPath)` on vault_presence's data. This removes the string-concat scan and centralizes the delimiter so it isn't re-implemented in selection/drag code.
- **D26 — Cull tuning constants and the group→keeper pipeline live inline in an AppState closure instead of a Core policy/façade** (`AppState.swift:245-293`, api-design/M). The three cull strategies (bursts windowMs:60_000/cosine:0.93, duplicates hamming:2, similar hamming:6 — AppState.swift:255,260,265) and the entire group→fetch-items→measure-sharpness→pick-keeper assembly (AppState.swift:267-288) are hand-written inline in one Task.detached closure in the App layer. The domain knowledge of 'what is a burst/duplicate/similar group and how to rank it' lives in the UI target, not in Core. Consequences: these magic numbers are untestable and undiscoverable (the unit tests pass their own thresholds, so the SHIPPED thresholds have no coverage); the per-mode branching (sharpness only for .bursts, two phash thresholds) is duplicated control flow; and any new cull mode means editing a god-object closure. The 0.93 burst cosine is also applied to MobileCLIP SCENE embeddings reused from semantic search — a reuse decision buried at the call site with no abstraction documenting it. *Change:* Introduce a Core-level `CullService` (or extend LibraryService) exposing `groups(mode:) -> [CullGroup-equivalent]`, owning the thresholds as a `CullPolicy` value (per-mode window/threshold constants) and the group→keeper assembly. AppState calls one façade method and only maps results to view models. Move CullGroup's pure parts into Core. This makes shipped thresholds test-targetable and gives new modes a single extension point.
- **D27 — Binary success/failure return collapses error taxonomy and conflates 'no result' with 'done'** (`DerivationStage.swift:16`, error-model/M). `run(...) -> Bool` flattens every outcome into success/retryable-failure. The runner increments attempts and gives up after 3 on ANY false (markDerivationFailed, Catalog+Derivation.swift:53). But the stages already need a third outcome and fake it: EmbedStage/Face/OCR return false for BOTH a transient/unreadable error AND a genuinely-broken file — a permanently corrupt asset wastes 3 retries and then is silently dropped with no diagnosis; meanwhile GeocodeStage returns `true` for 'no GPS / no nearby city' (GeocodeStage.swift:34,39) to avoid retries, overloading 'success' to mean 'analyzed, produced nothing'. There is no recorded reason for a failure (the job stores only status+attempts), so a user with N permanently-failing photos has no way to see why, and the catalog cannot distinguish 'analyzed, empty' from 'not yet analyzed' except by the side-effect table existing. This limits observability and any future 'show me what failed and why' UI. *Change:* Replace `-> Bool` with a typed result, e.g. `enum StageOutcome { case completed, skipped(reason), failedTransient(Error), failedPermanent(Error) }`. The runner maps completed/skipped → done (no retry), failedTransient → attempts++ (retry-capped), failedPermanent → mark terminal immediately (don't burn 3 attempts) and store the reason. Add a nullable `lastError`/`reason` column to derivation_jobs (documented format change → update docs/format catalog notes per CLAUDE.md). This also lets GeocodeStage say `.completed` for 'no city found' honestly instead of overloading true.
- **D28 — Per-stage eligibility/kind/GPS predicates duplicated and hardcoded between catalog and stages** (`Catalog+Derivation.swift:9`, duplication/S). A stage's selection predicate is split across two places that must be kept in lockstep by hand. Catalog.eligibleKind(forStage:) hardcodes a string switch over 'ocr'/'embed'/'faces'/'geocode'/'phash' (Catalog+Derivation.swift:9-18) that just returns 'photo' for everything, duplicating each stage's own `eligibleKind` (DerivationStage). Worse, the geocode-specific 'has lat/lon' filter is special-cased by literal `if stage == "geocode"` in BOTH pendingDerivation (Catalog+Derivation.swift:32) and derivationProgress (line 70). Adding a stage with a different eligible kind (e.g. video transcript/scene) or a different precondition (e.g. only assets with EXIF) requires editing the catalog's hardcoded switch and adding another `if stage ==` branch, rather than declaring it on the stage. This is a coupling/extensibility hazard precisely where the roadmap (more intelligence stages) will grow. *Change:* Make the stage the single source of truth for its selection predicate. Move `eligibleKind` to drive the query (it already exists on DerivationStage) and replace the geocode `if stage ==` special-cases with a stage-supplied SQL precondition, e.g. add `var pendingPredicate: String { "" }` (or a small typed enum like `.requiresColumns(["latitude","longitude"])`) to DerivationStage; GeocodeStage returns the lat/lon-not-null clause. pendingDerivation/derivationProgress take the stage (or its descriptor) instead of a bare string and compose kind+predicate from it, deleting Catalog.eligibleKind(forStage:).
- **D29 — Single serial drain of all stages with no batching or bounded parallelism** (`AppState.swift:1475`, concurrency-architecture/M). drainDerivation iterates stages outer-serially (AppState.swift:1475) and, within a stage, processes the entire pending set one asset at a time, awaiting each `Task.detached(.utility)` before starting the next (AppState.swift:1489-1508). For each asset the per-stage cost includes a FULL-RES image decode (CGImageSourceCreateImageAtIndex) plus a 256x256 32BGRA CVPixelBuffer (EmbedStage.makePixelBuffer) plus an MLMultiArray and the MLModel.prediction. Because stages are independent and each re-decodes the same source file, a single 10k-photo import re-decodes every file up to ~4 times (ocr/embed/faces/phash all needsFile) and uses only one core for inference, leaving the machine's parallelism idle. There is no concurrency cap, no per-asset decode sharing across stages, and no batching of catalog writes; on the documented ~10k acceptance import this is the throughput ceiling. (Memory per item is bounded since it is strictly serial — this is the space/throughput tradeoff, not an OOM.) *Change:* In the extracted DerivationRunner, (a) pivot the loop to per-asset: for each pending asset decode the CGImage ONCE and pass it to all file-backed stages that need it (change DerivationStage.run to optionally accept an already-decoded CGImage/source, or add a `run(asset:decoded:)` overload), eliminating 3–4x redundant decodes; and (b) introduce a bounded-concurrency drain (e.g. a small TaskGroup with a width tuned to cores, or process N assets concurrently) while keeping the whole-pending-set fetch so starvation stays fixed. Keep Vision/CLIP each single-flighted if the model isn't reentrant, but overlap decode with inference. Optionally batch markDerived writes.
- **D30 — Dedup identity is fragmented across three unrelated fingerprint schemes; the registry's own fingerprint is never used by the engine** (`ImportRegistry.swift:25`, data-model/M). Three different notions of 'is this already here' coexist with no shared abstraction. (1) The ENGINE's authoritative dedup is content-hash + folder via `catalog.hashPresent(vault,dirPath,hash)` after re-hashing the staged copy (ImportEngine.swift:93). (2) The IMPORT REGISTRY keys on `sourceKey|name|size|takenAt` (ImportRegistry.swift:25,55) — but `registry.contains(...)` is consulted ONLY by the UI to gray out already-imported items (ImportView.swift:350, FreeUpPhoneView.swift:28); the engine never calls it, so the registry's fingerprint and the engine's dedup are entirely disconnected. (3) The UI's 'already in library' glyph uses yet a third fingerprint: `knownSizeDateKeys` (size|capture-second) plus, for foreign drives, exact `assetHashes` (ImportView.swift:365-377). Consequence: the meaning of 'duplicate' differs by code path, the size+second heuristic can false-positive/negative independently of the hash truth, and a maintainer changing one scheme has no single place that defines item identity. The registry fingerprint in particular pretends to be a dedup key but is decorative. *Change:* Define one `ImportIdentity` concept with two explicit tiers and make every path name which tier it uses: a cheap pre-flight tier (used only for UI hints before any copy — size+capture-second and source-claimed hash) and the authoritative tier (post-hash content identity, the only thing that gates an actual import/skip). Centralize the cheap pre-flight in a single helper the UI and FreeUpPhoneView share, and document that the registry is an audit/provenance log, not a dedup oracle — or, if it is meant to gate imports, route the engine's skip decision through it consistently. Keep `hashPresent` as the sole gate for real skips.
- **D31 — Per-batch verify reads the entire manifest into a dictionary and triggers a whole-vault rescan** (`ImportEngine.swift:136`, concurrency-architecture/L). After placing a batch, the engine calls `library.rescan(vaultID:)` which runs a full-vault Scanner pass (LibraryService.swift:350-355), then reads the ENTIRE manifest.jsonl and builds a `[path: hash]` dictionary over every asset in the vault just to verify the handful of files it placed (ImportEngine.swift:145-146). Both costs are O(vault size), not O(batch size). With the UI driving imports as multiple batches per session, a large library pays a full rescan + full-manifest parse per batch. This makes batching pessimal — smaller batches (better UI progress) cost MORE total work — which structurally discourages the responsive incremental import the 10k acceptance test needs. *Change:* Verify against only the placed paths: either (a) have the scanner/rescan return the manifest entries it just (re)wrote for the placed files, or (b) compute the verification hash for the placed copies directly (the engine already trusts its own staging hash; re-reading the placed file's manifest line is the independence check — fetch just those lines via an indexed manifest lookup rather than a full dictionary build). Long-term, give the scanner an incremental 'scan these N paths' entry point so per-batch cost is O(batch), and let the registry/verify read individual manifest entries instead of materializing the whole file.
- **D32 — Takeout JSON resolution is an un-indexed per-file filesystem stat storm, repeated up to 3× per media file** (`TakeoutJSONMatcher.swift:35`, concurrency-architecture/M). For every media file, `TakeoutJSONMatcher.jsonURL` builds 6+ candidate JSON names and probes each with `FileManager.fileExists` until one hits (TakeoutJSONMatcher.swift:35-41) — a fresh stat() per candidate, worst case all 6+ when no JSON exists. Worse, this whole probe runs up to three times for the same file: during enumeration via `bestTakenAt` (TakeoutSource.swift:108) and again at fetch time (line 63), plus `looksLikeTakeout`. There is no per-directory JSON index. On a 10k-file Takeout that is ~tens of thousands of redundant stat()s, single-threaded inside `enumerateItems` (no bounded concurrency, unlike VolumeSource which at least parallelizes EXIF reads 8-wide). The matching is not the O(files·json-list) linear scan the brief feared — there is no JSON list iterated — but the un-indexed, un-cached, repeated stat pattern produces the same enumerate-is-slow symptom. *Change:* Build a one-pass directory index during enumeration: while walking the tree, bucket every `.json` filename by directory into `[dirURL: Set<String>]`, then resolve each media file's JSON by checking candidate names against the in-memory set (string ops, zero stat). Cache the resolved media→JSON URL (and the parsed `TakeoutMetadata`) on the source so fetch reuses enumeration's result instead of re-probing and re-parsing. Optionally parallelize the parse pass with the same bounded TaskGroup VolumeSource already uses, to make Takeout enumeration consistent with the volume path.
- **D33 — Eviction/rehydrate verify via whole-drive presence fetch + per-item linear scan (O(items × drive_rows))** (`LibraryService+Eviction.swift:132-145`, data-model/S). `verifyOnCanonical`, `driveSource`, and the rehydrate Live-pair lookup all resolve a single (vault, hash) by calling `catalog.vaultPresenceRows(forVault:)` — which `SELECT`s and materializes every presence row for the entire drive — and then `.first(where: { $0.hash == ... })`. In `evict`, `verifyOnCanonical` runs per item (and per connected canonical drive), so binning N photos against a drive of R rows is roughly O(N × R) row loads plus N full-table fetches; `rehydrate` repeats the pattern for each half. On a multi-thousand-photo canonical drive this turns a batch evict into many full presence-table scans. The structural cause is a missing point-lookup query: the data model exposes only a fetch-all accessor for what are logically keyed (vaultID, hash) lookups. *Change:* Add an indexed point query `presenceRow(forVault:hash:) -> VaultPresenceEntry?` (SELECT ... WHERE vaultID = ? AND hash = ? LIMIT 1, backed by an index on vault_presence(vaultID, hash)) and route `verifyOnCanonical`/`driveSource`/rehydrate Live-pair resolution through it. For true batch operations, optionally add `presenceRows(forVault:hashes:)` returning a `[hash: row]` map so one query serves a whole evict batch.
- **D34 — ingestSidecars re-reads the entire manifest after every rescan, regardless of what changed** (`LibraryService.swift:70-80`, abstraction/M). `rescan(vaultID:)` — invoked after every delete, restore, evict, rehydrate, rename, and move — runs the scanner off-main but then calls `ingestSidecars(vault:)` synchronously on the caller's context. `ingestSidecars` reads the full `manifest.jsonl`, and for each entry opens+decodes the XMP sidecar and writes a per-hash `updateHumanMetadata` row. So a single-file delete triggers a whole-library sidecar re-ingest (O(library) file reads + DB writes). This conflates two concerns (scan-the-vault vs. mirror-sidecars) at a coarse grain and makes every small mutation pay a library-sized metadata pass, much of it on the main thread when rescan is awaited from a main-actor method. *Change:* Either fold sidecar ingest into the Scanner pass it already shadows (the scanner walks the same manifest), or make ingest incremental — ingest only the entries the scan reports as added/changed, or expose `ingestSidecar(forHash:)` for the single-asset mutation paths (rename/move/delete touch known hashes). Run the ingest inside the same `Task.detached(.utility)` block as the scan so it never lands on main.
- **D35 — FolderWatcher triggers an unscoped whole-library rescan; no path-to-vault routing or coalescing of bursts** (`FolderWatcher.swift:28-43`, api-design/M). The watcher's `onChange` is a zero-argument `() -> Void` — it discards the changed `eventPaths` entirely (they're only used to classify all-internal vs not). AppState wires it to `rescan()` → `scanAll`, which re-walks every vault and reloads each full manifest on any single-file change. The debounce (2s, coalesced via DispatchWorkItem) is correct, but because the callback carries no path information, even a one-file change forces an O(files)+O(manifest) full pass. This couples the watcher to a coarse 'rescan everything' policy and makes the fast-path's per-file cheapness moot at the directory-walk level. It also bypasses the AppState.scanning re-entrancy guard's intent under rapid edits since each fire schedules a fresh full scan. *Change:* Change the watcher callback to `(Set<String> changedPaths) -> Void` and route changed paths to the owning vault, so the dispatcher can trigger a scoped incremental scan of just the affected subtrees/vaults rather than `scanAll`. Pair with a `Scanner.scan(vault:scope:)` overload (subtree-limited enumerator) once the streaming refactor exists. Keep the all-internal `.openphoto/` filter. This makes the 'cheap incremental rescan' the watcher's doc comment promises actually cheap.
- **D36 — Scanner is a stateless free function with no concurrency guard or seam for testing/extension** (`Scanner.swift:3-18`, testability/M). `Scanner` is an enum with one static async function that hard-depends on `FileManager.default`, `Manifest.read/write`, `ContentHash`, `MetadataExtractor`, and concrete `Catalog`. There's no protocol seam for the filesystem or hashing, so unit tests must build a real on-disk vault + real GRDB catalog to exercise any path (fast-path hit/miss, skip-on-error, pairing integration). More importantly, nothing prevents two scans of the same vault overlapping: `scanAll` is guarded only by the UI-level `AppState.scanning` flag, but `rescan(vaultID:)` is also invoked from `restore`/bin-delete flows (LibraryService) with no such guard, and both end in `replaceInstances` (DELETE+insert). Concurrent scans of one vault could interleave a DELETE between another's read and write. The stateless-function shape leaves no obvious home for a per-vault scan lock. *Change:* Promote Scanner to an injectable type (or keep the static API but add a `ScanContext` holding a FileWalker/Hasher protocol) so tests can drive it with an in-memory FS and a fake catalog. Add a per-vault serialization point — e.g. an actor or async lock keyed by vaultID in LibraryService — so scanAll and rescan(vaultID:) can't run the same vault's reconcile concurrently. This also gives the streaming refactor a natural owner.
- **D37 — Lossy error model: Bool/optional-try swallow the reason exactly where the format spec wants it recorded** (`VerifiedCopy.swift:10 (returns Bool, no reason)`, error-model/M). The transfer layer collapses every distinct failure cause into a Boolean or a swallowed optional-try. VerifiedCopy.copy returns false identically for 'dest already exists', 'hash mismatch (bit-rot/corruption in source)', 'disk full', and 'I/O error'. SyncEngine.plan explicitly notes it cannot distinguish an unreadable destination from a hash mismatch ('Distinguishing the two needs a reason field, out of scope for Slice 1', :34-36) and so conservatively buckets both as conflicts. SyncResult.failed and conflicts are bare [PlanItem] with no cause. SendEngine.run flattens any thrown error from destination.send into the literal string 'send failed' (:50). The user-facing consequence is that the UI cannot tell 'this drive is full' from 'this file is corrupt' from 'this path already differs', and the sync-log records only counts. This directly undercuts the project's third-party/server-readable canonical-drive goal: the format docs want machine-readable reasons, but the engine has none to write. *Change:* Introduce a TransferFailure enum (alreadyPresentDifferent, hashMismatch(expected,got), unreadableSource, unreadableDest, insufficientSpace, io(Error)) and have VerifiedCopy return Result<Void, TransferFailure> (or throw it). Carry it on a failed-item struct (PlanItem + reason) in SyncResult/SendEngine.Result, and surface it in the sync-log line and the conflict UI. This also lets SyncEngine.plan finally split 'conflict' from 'unreadable', which it flags as deferred today.
- **D38 — Three sibling transfer engines with no shared copy-verify-record-journal abstraction** (`SyncEngine.swift:120 (apply)`, abstraction/M). SyncEngine.apply, SendEngine.run, and DeletionPropagator each independently re-implement the same four-phase pipeline: free-space/precheck → per-item verified-copy-or-bin → bucket into a result struct → append a hand-formatted sync-log summary string. Yet the copy-and-verify atom diverges: SyncEngine.apply and DriftReconciler use VerifiedCopy.copy, but VolumeCopyDestination.send hand-rolls its OWN copy+fsync+re-hash+cleanup (VolumeCopyDestination.swift:45-70) that duplicates VerifiedCopy's logic with subtly different cleanup (it overwrites via collisionFreeURL rather than never-overwrite). Each engine also defines a near-identical Progress struct (SyncProgress, SendProgress, DriftProgress — all {stage?, done, total, currentName}) and a near-identical Result struct (SyncResult, SendEngine.Result) with the same buckets under different names. The journaling is copy-pasted three ways (two of them via library.appendSyncLog with the special-cased mac-vs-drive both-ends logic inline in SyncEngine.apply:195-205, one via SyncLog.append directly in DeletionPropagator:86). This is maintainability debt and a correctness-divergence risk: a fix to the verified-copy or journaling rule must be made in 3-4 places. *Change:* Extract a shared transfer core: (1) make every byte-copy go through VerifiedCopy (give it a collisionFree/overwrite-allowed variant so VolumeCopyDestination drops its hand-rolled copy); (2) hoist a single TransferProgress {stage, done, total, currentName} and a generic TransferResult<Item> with confirmed/skipped/conflict/failed buckets, used by all three engines; (3) move the mac↔drive both-ends sync-log policy into one SyncJournal helper rather than inlining it in apply(). SyncEngine/SendEngine/DeletionPropagator then become thin orchestrators (plan → forEach VerifiedTransfer → journal) over the shared core.
- **D39 — AtomicFile's durability contract omits the parent-directory fsync the format spec mandates, weakening crash-consistency of the manifest rename on passive drives** (`AtomicFile.swift:6`, error-model/S).
