AtomicFile fsyncs the temp file's data (fh.synchronize, line 14) then calls FileManager.replaceItemAt (line 21). The data is durable but the *rename* (the directory entry change that makes the new manifest visible and removes the temp) is not fsync'd to the containing directory. The format doc §4/§10 specifies 'temp file -> fsync -> rename' as the atomicity contract third-party writers rely on, and the whole drive model is 'passive drives, crash-consistent after a sync'. On a power loss right after a sync rewrites manifest.jsonl on a removable drive, the directory metadata may not have reached stable storage, so the manifest could roll back to the pre-rename version while the copied originals are already on disk — exactly the 'manifest behind reality' drift the design treats as recoverable, but avoidable. replaceItemAt's own durability guarantees are also filesystem-dependent and undocumented in this code. This is the one place where 'atomic' is asserted but not fully delivered, and it is the single choke point every state write flows through, so the gap is systemic. *Change:* After the rename, open the destination's parent directory and fsync it (open(dir, O_RDONLY); fcntl/fsync; close), or use the lower-level rename(2)+fsync-dir sequence rather than replaceItemAt, and document the realized guarantee in a comment that cites format §10. Optionally expose a durability level (e.g. .barrier vs .relaxed) so hot-path catalog-adjacent writes can opt out while manifest/vault.json always barrier.
- **D40 — BinStore keys deletions by relative path, so two distinct deletions of the same path collide — losing recoverable bytes and making restore ambiguous** (`BinStore.swift:21`, data-model/M). moveToBin computes the bin destination as binDirURL.appendingPathComponent(relPath) with no collision handling (line 25), unlike every other placement path which routes through FileNaming.collisionFreeURL. If a file at rome2022/IMG_1.heic is deleted, a new different file later lands at the same path and is also deleted, the second moveItem targets an already-occupied bin slot: it throws (bin is left without the second file) or, depending on FileManager behavior, the records diverge. The bin.jsonl log (and restore at line 42, which filters purely by $0.path) then has two BinItems with identical path but different hash/deletedAt — restore(relPath:) picks the wrong bytes and removes the wrong log line. This violates the 'nothing hard-deletes; everything in the bin is recoverable' invariant precisely in the second-deletion case. The data model conflates 'logical path' with 'bin storage identity', when the durable identity is the content hash. *Change:* Store binned files content-addressed (bin/<hh>/<hash> like the thumbnail cache) or under a collision-free path, and make BinItem carry that storage key alongside the display path. Restore keys on (hash) or the storage key, not the bare relPath. This keeps the format doc's 'original relative path preserved' as a display/restore-target hint while giving each binned blob a unique slot. Bump/annotate format §8 in the same commit per the documentation-discipline rule.
- **D41 — Sidecar-per-file model has no batch/streaming abstraction, forcing ingest and export to be O(N) sequential single-file opens on the main scan path** (`SidecarStore.swift:8`, abstraction/M). SidecarStore exposes only single-file read(forMediaRelPath:)/write(forMediaRelPath:). ingestSidecars (LibraryService:70) and SidecarExporter (line 13) therefore iterate the entire manifest and, for every entry, build a URL, stat for existence, open+read the file, and run a full XMLDocument parse — N file opens and N XML parses, sequentially, with no parallelism or skip-index. Because the format says 'a sidecar exists only if there is something to record', the vast majority of those N stats hit nothing, yet ingest still pays the per-entry catalog round-trip cost. ingestSidecars runs after *every* scan and rescan (called from scanAll and rescan after every delete/restore/rename), so a single deletion in a 50k-asset vault triggers a 50k-entry sidecar sweep. There is no abstraction that says 'give me the human metadata for these N hashes' or 'iterate only sidecars that exist', so the cost is structural, not incidental. *Change:* Add a directory-driven enumeration to SidecarStore (e.g. enumerateSidecars(under:) that walks the per-folder .openphoto dirs and yields only present sidecars), and a batch ingest that diffs against catalog state so a no-op rescan does ~0 sidecar work. Drive XML parsing through a reusable parser and run the sweep on a bounded-parallel TaskGroup off the main path (matches the documented Task.detached(.utility) model and the indexing memory-safety memo). Keep single-file read/write for the edit path.
- **D42 — The read-append-atomic-rewrite pattern is duplicated across five append-only JSONL files instead of one shared append-log abstraction** (`SyncLog.swift:5`, duplication/M). Five independent JSONL files (sync-log, bin, imports, sends, devices) each hand-roll the same logic: read the whole file, decode every line, append/merge, re-encode every line, AtomicFile.write the whole file. SyncLog.append (line 12) and BinStore.writeLog (line 70) do a literal full read+rewrite on every single append. The format doc explicitly calls sync-log.jsonl and imports.jsonl 'append-only journals' yet none of them actually append — each is O(M) per write and imports.jsonl is documented (§12) as permanent and never-pruned, so it grows unbounded while every import re-serializes the entire history. Five near-identical implementations also means five places to get atomicity/encoding/NFC wrong independently (e.g. SyncLog swallows all errors with try?, BinStore throws). *Change:* Extract an AppendLog<Entry: Codable> (or JSONLStore) that encapsulates: lazy whole-file load into an index, O(1) in-memory append/merge, and a flush policy. For the genuinely append-only logs (sync-log, imports, sends, devices) implement a true append (open for append, write one line + fsync) and reserve full atomic rewrite only for compaction. Have BinStore, SyncLog, and the three registries become thin typed wrappers over it. ManifestStore from the prior finding can share the same base for its full-rewrite flush.
### Low

- **D43 — Float16 embedding pack/unpack helpers duplicated across catalog extensions** (`Catalog+Embeddings.swift:6-18`, duplication/S). packFloat16/unpackFloat16 (Catalog+Embeddings.swift:6-18) and packF16/unpackF16 (Catalog+Faces.swift:30-42) are byte-for-byte the same little-endian Float16 codec, copy-pasted with a comment admitting the duplication to 'avoid collision'. This is the on-disk encoding for every embedding and face vector — the format that a future server/third-party consumer of the canonical drive must reproduce. Two copies means a fix or endianness/precision tweak can drift between faces and embeddings, silently corrupting one vector store. Low severity only because they are currently identical and the catalog is rebuildable. *Change:* Extract one internal `Float16Vector` codec (e.g. enum with pack(_:)/unpack(_:dim:)) in Core, used by both extensions. Since this is the normative on-disk vector encoding, document it in docs/format/ (catalog-schema) per the project's documentation-discipline invariant.
- **D44 — Stage conformance pattern is inconsistent (enum-static vs final-class vs struct wrapper)** (`OCRStage.swift:5`, abstraction/S). The five stages use three different shapes for the same role: OCRStage/FaceStage are `enum` namespaces of static funcs with a SEPARATE struct wrapper (OCRDerivationStage/FaceDerivationStage) that conforms to DerivationStage; EmbedStage/GeocodeStage are `final class @unchecked Sendable` that conform directly; PHashStage is a `final class` whose `run` just calls a free `PerceptualHash.compute`. This inconsistency means a contributor adding a stage has no canonical template, the `id` constant is declared twice in some stages (e.g. FaceStage.id and FaceDerivationStage.id both 'faces'), and `@unchecked Sendable` is used where a value type or actor would give checked safety. It is cosmetic today but raises the cost of the (roadmapped) growth in stages. *Change:* Settle on one canonical shape: a small value-type (struct) or actor `XStage: DerivationStage` that owns any model/state, with pure inference helpers as private statics or free functions in the same file. Fold the enum+wrapper duplication (OCR/Face) into a single type, deriving `id` once. Prefer an actor for stages that hold compiled models (Embed) so `@unchecked Sendable` can be dropped. Document the template in docs as the 'how to add a derivation stage' recipe.
- **D45 — CameraSource concurrency model is well-designed (no change recommended)** (`CameraSource.swift:20`, concurrency-architecture/S). Called out as a positive. The ICC adapter handles a genuinely hostile substrate (delegate callbacks on ICC's own queue, unreliable object handles, locked-device session dance, stale-session -21347 recovery) with disciplined, well-documented invariants: single-flight enumeration coalescing (CameraSource.swift:131) to stop concurrent reads from corrupting the shared non-Sendable map, atomic local-map build then publish under lock, copy-out-then-resume continuation discipline to avoid re-entrancy deadlock, and the extraction of `CameraIdentity` into a pure, unit-testable function precisely because `ICDevice` can't be constructed off hardware. This is the right boundary and the right amount of comment density for code that can't be exercised in CI. *Change:* No structural change. Keep the THIN-adapter discipline. The only latent risk worth a note (not a refactor): the lock-guarded single-continuation model assumes the engine never issues two fetches concurrently to one CameraSource; that contract is documented but enforced only by convention — a `// precondition: single-flight` assertion or a serial executor would make the assumption self-checking if a future caller violates it.
- **D46 — Selection layer is well-structured; per-tap firstIndex scan is the only minor hotspot** (`SelectionModel.swift:17`, testability/S). This is mostly a 'well-designed, leave it' note. `SelectionModel` is a pure `Sendable` value type with a `Set<String>` backing (correct choice — membership/toggle/range are all O(1)/O(range), and partner mirroring is handled atomically); `tap` range is O(range), `updateDrag` is one O(P) frame scan, not the O(K·P) the brief hypothesized. `UndoAction` holds only hashes/relPaths and replays through existing public ops, with depth capped by the native UndoManager (50) — undo memory is bounded by design. The only real costs are at the call sites, not in the model: `orderedSelectable` rebuilds a full `[SelectableItem]` array on every TimelineView render, and each tap does `state.flatItems.firstIndex(where: instanceID == ...)` (O(P) per tap) to recover the index the cell already knows about. *Change:* Cache `orderedSelectable` and an `instanceID → index` map alongside `flatItems` (rebuild only when flatItems changes) so tap is O(1) index lookup and renders don't re-map. Optionally give the cell its row index directly so no lookup is needed. No change to the (good) SelectionModel/UndoAction types themselves.
- **D47 — Well-designed leaf components (note explicitly): pairing, hashing, metadata pooling, value types** (`LivePhotoPairer.swift:24-65`, abstraction/S). Not a defect — recording the parts of the subsystem that are structurally sound so the refactors above preserve them. `LivePhotoPairer.pair` is a pure O(n) function (two hash-map passes: contentIdentifier match, then dir|basename fallback — not O(n^2)), order-independent and trivially testable. `ContentHash.ofFile` streams in 1MB chunks with a per-chunk autoreleasepool for genuine constant memory. `MetadataExtractor.extractImage` and `EmbeddedMetadata.read` correctly wrap ImageIO in autoreleasepool (the memory-OOM remediation). `MediaKind`, `MediaMetadata`, `ManifestEntry` are clean Sendable value types with the on-disk keys pinned to the format. These abstractions are at the right altitude and should be left intact. *Change:* No change. When implementing the streaming/parallel refactor, keep these as the pure leaf functions they are — feed batches through `LivePhotoPairer.pair` (it already operates on a full candidate list and can run once at the end), and reuse `ContentHash`/`MetadataExtractor` unchanged inside the TaskGroup workers. Preserve the per-file autoreleasepool boundary under parallelism.
- **D48 — CatalogSnapshot read paths re-open and full-table-scan the snapshot DB independently** (`CatalogSnapshot.swift:71 (import)`, duplication/M). There are three separate read entry points into a drive snapshot — import (assets + presence + thumbnails), assetDates (hash→takenAtMs SELECT *), and PeekSource.load (which spins up a whole temp Catalog and calls CatalogSnapshot.import just to enumerate timeline items for a read-only peek). Each opens its own read-only DatabaseQueue and does a full SELECT over assets. The snapshot 'reader' contract (documented in catalog-schema.md per the comments) is implicit and scattered across these call sites rather than embodied in one SnapshotReader type, so a schema change to the portable tables must be tracked across three places, and PeekSource pays the cost of a full catalog import + a temp SQLite file for what is conceptually a read-only listing. *Change:* Introduce a single SnapshotReader(drive:) value that owns the read-only DatabaseQueue and exposes the portable surface (assets(), presence(forVault:), assetDates(), timelineRows()). import/assetDates/PeekSource all go through it. PeekSource's snapshot backend then reads timeline rows directly from the reader instead of importing into a throwaway Catalog. This also gives the documented third-party reader contract exactly one implementation to match the format docs.
- **D49 — Per-item full presence-table scan in send-source resolution** (`LibraryService+SendSource.swift:44`, data-model/S). resolveSendSources calls driveSource(forHash:among:) once per drive-only item, and driveSource fetches the ENTIRE vault_presence row set for each connected drive (catalog.vaultPresenceRows) and does a linear .first(where: hash ==) scan — repeated per item, per drive. Selecting K drive-only items across D drives is O(K·D·P) catalog reads + scans (full table materialized K·D times). Fine for a handful of selected items; pathological for a 'send 2000 drive-only photos' batch. It also re-reads the same presence rows the caller may already hold. *Change:* Resolve drive sources in one pass: build a [hash: (vault, row)] index once from the connected drives' presence rows (canonical-first so the first writer wins), then look up each item O(1). Equivalently add a catalog query that returns presence rows for a SET of hashes across vaults in a single SQL IN(...) read.
- **D50 — Format-coupled timestamp and path-normalization logic is scattered as free helpers rather than centralized, risking divergence in the canonical on-disk representation** (`VaultDescriptor.swift:41`, coupling/S). The format's canonical-form rules — ISO-8601-millis timestamps, NFC path normalization, '/'-separated vault-relative paths — are implemented as several independent helpers: ISO8601Millis (VaultDescriptor.swift), Vault.relativePath (resolvesSymlinks + NFC), VaultReorganizer.norm (NFC + slash-trim), SyncEngine.driveRelPath (manual concat + NFC). They mostly agree but each re-derives 'what canonical looks like'. ISO8601Millis even carries a lenient parser to tolerate a self-inflicted ambiguity (writer emits fractional seconds, some readers don't), a sign the canonical encoding isn't owned in one place. Because the format spec is normative for an external server consumer, any drift between these helpers (e.g. a path that one normalizes and another doesn't) becomes an interop bug that is hard to attribute. *Change:* Collect canonical-form encoding into a single VaultFormat (or CanonicalPath/CanonicalTime) namespace: one path normalizer (NFC + separator + relative resolution), one timestamp encode/decode pair, used by Manifest, BinStore, SyncEngine, VaultReorganizer, and the registries. Make ManifestEntry/BinItem construct paths only via that normalizer so an un-normalized path cannot be persisted. This also gives the format doc a single code anchor.

---

## 9. Appendix — Scale model, hot paths & index coverage

_(from Investigation B's scale-model mapper.)_


### Scale model

OpenPhoto's cost is driven by a small set of countable quantities. Mapped to this codebase:

| Param | Maps to | Where it lives |
|---|---|---|
| **N** | Total catalogued assets (distinct `assets.hash`, photos + videos). The dominant term for every browse/scan/derivation pass. | `assets` table |
| **M** | Local **instances** = (asset × local vault) rows. M ≥ N because the same hash can appear in two local vaults (intentional v1 dup); `instances` is keyed `(vaultID, relPath)`. | `instances` table |
| **F** | Distinct folders / `dirPath` values on the Mac. Drives `folderTree`, `folderCounts`, folder filters. | `instances.dirPath`, `vault_presence.dirPath` |
| **V** | Number of registered vaults (1 local + connected/known drives). Multiplies presence rows and sync sources. | `vaults` table |
| **D** | **Drive-only** presence rows = assets on a drive with no local instance. Each adds a `vault_presence` row and a row to the timeline UNION's drive branch. | `vault_presence` table |
| **E** | Embeddings present (CLIP image vectors, ≤ N photos). Sizes the in-memory `SemanticIndex` matrix (E × dim fp32) and the brute-force search `vDSP_mmul`. | `embeddings` table |
| **P** | Pending derivation jobs across stages (ocr/embed/faces/geocode/phash) — the unstarted/failed-retryable work the drain must traverse. Worst case ≈ 5·N at first index. | `derivation_jobs` + `pendingDerivation` |
| **T** | OCR text corpus (recognized-text rows in the FTS5 `ocr` table, ≤ N photos). Sizes full-text search. | `ocr` virtual table |
| **K** | Detected faces (≈ a few × N for people-heavy libraries); of those, **U** = unassigned auto faces feeds the clusterer. | `faces` table |
| **B** | Geotagged assets (assets with non-null lat/lon, ≤ N). Drives the Map surface + grid clustering. | `assets.latitude/longitude`, `geocode` |

**Three reference sizes** (N = catalogued assets; others scale roughly with N):

- **10k** — single user, one local vault, maybe one backup drive. N≈10k, M≈N, F≈hundreds, E/T/B a fraction of N, K≈10–30k. Everything fits comfortably in memory; full-library in-Swift passes are fine.
- **100k** — the realistic "friend's real import" target (the live acceptance test). N≈100k, F≈1–5k, K≈100–300k, E≈80k. In-memory full-library materializations (timeline UNION → `[TimelineItem]`, `SemanticIndex` matrix, face clustering) start to cost real seconds/RAM. This is the size the memory-safety work (autorelease pools, autorelease OOM) was provoked by.
- **1M** — stress ceiling / multi-drive archive. N≈1M, D potentially large (cold-storage drives), E≈1M × dim fp32 (hundreds of MB resident), K in the millions, F≈10k+. Several hot paths here are O(N) full scans or O(N²)/O(N·k) Swift loops that will not hold; this is where the deferred tile-grid renderer and the un-indexed timeline UNION become the bottlenecks.

### Hot-path inventory

The ~14 most performance-critical operations, where they live, and the dominant parameter:

| # | Operation | Location | Dominant param | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Vault scan** (walk → fast-path manifest match → hash new → extract metadata → replace instances) | `Scanner/Scanner.swift:17` (walk loop :29; hash loop :63; extract :91) | **M** (walk + manifest dict) + **(new files)** for hashing/extract | `oldByPath` dict is O(M); `knownHashes()` pulls all N hashes into a `Set`. Metadata extract is per-new-file I/O. Single-threaded; the residual memory-safety item. |
| 2 | **Derivation drain** (per stage, pull whole pending set, run inference off-main) | `AppState.swift:1473` (loop :1489); SQL `Catalog+Derivation.swift:23` | **P** (≈ 5·N worst case) | Pulls the *entire* pending set per stage up front (anti-starvation). `pendingDerivation` is a `LEFT JOIN assets×derivation_jobs` + `ORDER BY takenAtMs DESC` per stage. |
| 3 | **refreshQueries** (timeline sections + folder tree + bin) | `AppState.swift:1531` | **N + M + D + F** | Materializes the whole timeline UNION into `flatItems`, rebuilds the folder tree, reads bin. The single most-called heavy main-actor entry; runs the union three different ways. |
| 4 | **Timeline browse** (the UNION of local instances ∪ drive-only) | `Catalog/Queries.swift:30` `timelineSQL`; `timelineItems` :33; `timelineSections` `LibraryService.swift:88` | **N + M + D** | UNION ALL of `localSelect` (assets⋈instances) and `driveSelect`. Then grouped in Swift (`groupedSections` :98) — O(result) with a `Calendar.dateInterval` call per item. |
| 5 | **Folder items** (`items(inDir:recursive:)`) | `Catalog/Queries.swift:61` | **M + D** filtered by **F** | Wraps `timelineSQL` in a subquery and filters on `dirPath = ?` / `dirPath GLOB ?/*` — the GLOB recursive case can't use the dirPath index. |
| 6 | **folderCounts / folderTree** | `Catalog/Queries.swift:101`; `LibraryService.folderTree:178` | **M + D** (counts) + **F** (tree build) | Two `GROUP BY dirPath` passes (local + drive-only, the drive branch carries the correlated `MIN(rowid)` subquery), then a filesystem walk (`directoriesUnder` :150) to surface empty dirs, then O(F) tree assembly. |
| 7 | **Structured filter** (Search facets) | `Search/Catalog+Search.swift:10` | **N + M + D**, amplified by filter predicates | Builds a WHERE over the full `timelineSQL` union. People/places/text become `hash IN (SELECT …)` subqueries; tags become `EXISTS(json_each(tagsJSON))` — none index-backed. |
| 8 | **Text search** (OCR FTS5 + caption/tag LIKE) | `Search/Catalog+Search.swift:113`; `searchOCR` `Catalog+Derivation.swift:90` | **T** (FTS5) + **N** (LIKE lane) | FTS5 `ocr MATCH … ORDER BY rank` is fast; the second lane is `caption LIKE %q%` + `json_each` LIKE over **all assets** — full scan. |
| 9 | **Semantic search** (build index + brute-force query) | `Search/SemanticIndex.swift:11` (build), `:28` (query); driver `AppState.runSearch:476` | **E** | Builds an E×dim fp32 matrix in RAM on `semanticIndexDirty`, then `vDSP_mmul` over all E rows + a full sort per query. No ANN; linear in E. |
| 10 | **Sync plan** (diff sources vs drive manifest) | `Sync/SyncEngine.swift:14` (`planClone` :74) | **M per source × V sources** | Reads every source + drive manifest; per source entry a dict lookup, plus a `ContentHash.ofFile` re-hash for any on-disk-but-unrecorded dest collision (I/O-bound worst case). |
| 11 | **Drift scan / verify** | `Sync/DriftReconciler.swift:27` (fast scan), `:134` (full verify) | **(files on drive ≈ N)** | `walk()` enumerates the whole drive into a dict; fast `scan` is size+mtime only; `verify` re-hashes *every* file (O(bytes)) — the slow path. `writeManifestEntry` rewrites the whole manifest per call (O(M) each). |
| 12 | **Face clustering** | `Faces/FaceClusterer.swift:28`; caller `AppState.swift:216` | **U** (unassigned auto faces) | Greedy single-link agglomerative, single-link membership test ⇒ worst case **O(U²·dim)**; `unassignedFacesWithEmbeddings` unpacks all U vectors from Float16 blobs first. The sharpest super-linear path. |
| 13 | **Tile / thumbnail load** | `Tiles/ThumbnailImage.swift:21` (cache+task :39); `Thumbnails/ThumbnailStore.swift:45` (`displayImage`) | **(visible cells)** bounded; **N** for first-pass generation | One shared `NSCache` cap 6000 decoded tiles. Per cell: sync cache read, else detached decode of the on-disk 512px JPEG. Known dense-grid GPU-texture hitch (deferred to Phase 5). |
| 14 | **Map grid clustering** | `Map/MapView.swift:351` (`cluster`); feed `geotaggedAssets` `Catalog+Geocode.swift:69` | **B** | `geotaggedAssets` loads all B rows; `cluster` buckets them into an 8×8 grid per region change (debounced, off-main). O(B) per recluster; centroid recompute per bucket. |

### Index coverage

Actual indexes created by the migrations (`Catalog.swift`), versus the predicates the hot queries actually filter/sort on. Flags mark full scans and correlated subqueries.

**Indexes that exist** (explicit `.indexed()` / `create(index:)` / primary keys):

| Table | Indexed columns | Source |
|---|---|---|
| `assets` | PK `hash`; `takenAtMs` (indexed) | v1 :41–:42 |
| `instances` | PK `(vaultID, relPath)`; `hash` (indexed); `dirPath` (indexed) | v1 :59–:66 |
| `vault_presence` | PK `(vaultID, hash)`; `hash` (indexed); `dirPath` (indexed) | v3 :82–:90 |
| `pending_deletions` | PK `hash` | v4 |
| `derivation_jobs` | PK `(hash, stage)` | v5 |
| `ocr` | FTS5 virtual (text indexed; `hash` notIndexed) | v5 :111 |
| `pending_folder_ops` | PK `id` (autoinc) | v6 |
| `embeddings` | PK `hash` | v7 |
| `people` | PK `id` | v8 |
| `faces` | PK `id`; `hash` (indexed); `personID` (indexed) | v8 :147–:159 |
| `geocode` | PK `hash`; `countryCode` (indexed); `idx_geocode_city` on `city` | v9 :165–:172 |
| `phash` | PK `hash` | v10 |
| `finder_tag_sync` | PK `hash` | v11 |

**No index on:** `assets.kind`, `assets.cameraModel`, `assets.favorite`, `assets.rating`, `assets.caption`, `assets.latitude/longitude`, `assets.isLivePairedVideo`, `assets.livePairHash`; `derivation_jobs.stage`/`status`; `faces.confidence`; `geocode.country`.

**Query → index coverage:**

| Query (file:line) | Filters / sorts on | Supporting index? | Flag |
|---|---|---|---|
| `timelineItems` / `timelineSQL` (`Queries.swift:30,33`) | join `instances.hash`→`assets.hash`, `assets.isLivePairedVideo=0`, `ORDER BY takenAtMs` | join uses `instances.hash` + `assets` PK; `takenAtMs` indexed; **but** `isLivePairedVideo` unindexed | **Partial** — outer `SELECT * FROM (union) ORDER BY takenAtMs` re-sorts the materialized union (no index across a UNION ALL). The `driveSelect` carries a **correlated subquery** `vp.rowid = (SELECT MIN(rowid) … WHERE v2.hash=a.hash)` + `NOT EXISTS(instances)`. |
| `items(inDir:)` non-recursive (`Queries.swift:61`) | `dirPath = ?` | `instances.dirPath` / `vault_presence.dirPath` indexed | **OK** for the base tables, but applied *after* the union subquery is materialized → index benefit is lost on the union wrapper. |
| `items(inDir: recursive)` (`Queries.swift:70`) | `dirPath GLOB '<d>/*'` | none usable | **Full scan** — GLOB with leading literal can't drive the index through the union; scans the union. |
| `folderCounts` local (`Queries.swift:106`) | `assets.isLivePairedVideo=0` [+ `kind='video'`], `GROUP BY i.dirPath` | `dirPath` indexed (group) | **Partial** — `isLivePairedVideo`/`kind` unindexed; full asset-join scan to filter. |
| `folderCounts` drive branch (`Queries.swift:122`) | `NOT EXISTS(instances)` + `vp.rowid = (SELECT MIN(rowid)…)` | hash indexed | **Correlated subquery** per row (the `MIN(rowid)` dedupe). |
| `structuredFilter` (`Catalog+Search.swift:10`) | over union: `takenAtMs`, `rating`, `favorite`, `kind`, `cameraModel IN`, `dirPath`, plus `IN/EXISTS` subqueries for tags/people/places/text | only `takenAtMs`, `dirPath` indexed | **Full scan** of the union for `rating`/`favorite`/`kind`/`cameraModel`; tags via `EXISTS(json_each(tagsJSON))` (**no index possible**); people/places/text via **`hash IN (SELECT …)` subqueries**. |
| `textMatches` LIKE lane (`Catalog+Search.swift:125`) | `caption LIKE %q%`, `json_each(tagsJSON) LIKE` | none | **Full scan** of `assets` (leading-wildcard LIKE + json_each). |
| `searchOCR` (`Catalog+Derivation.swift:97`) | `ocr MATCH ? ORDER BY rank` | FTS5 | **OK** (the one well-indexed text path). |
| `distinctCameras` / `distinctTags` (`Catalog+Search.swift:142,150`) | `DISTINCT cameraModel` / `DISTINCT json_each.value` | none | **Full scan** of `assets` (+ json_each fan-out for tags). |
| `pendingDerivation` (`Catalog+Derivation.swift:23`) | `LEFT JOIN derivation_jobs ON hash AND stage`, `assets.kind=?`, `isLivePairedVideo=0`, `j.status='failed'`, `ORDER BY takenAtMs` | join uses `derivation_jobs` PK `(hash,stage)`; `takenAtMs` indexed | **Partial** — `assets.kind`/`isLivePairedVideo` and `derivation_jobs.status` unindexed; full asset scan to find pending. |
| `derivationProgress` done count (`Catalog+Derivation.swift:74`) | `WHERE stage=? AND status='done'` | none (`derivation_jobs` only PK'd on `(hash,stage)`) | **Full scan** of `derivation_jobs` per stage (called repeatedly via `combinedProgress`). |
| `geotaggedAssets` (`Catalog+Geocode.swift:69`) | `latitude IS NOT NULL AND longitude IS NOT NULL`, `isLivePairedVideo=0`, `ORDER BY takenAtMs` | `takenAtMs` indexed; lat/lon unindexed | **Full scan** of `assets` to find the geotagged subset (B ≪ N but still scans N). |
| `distinctPlaces` (`Catalog+Geocode.swift:82`) | `GROUP BY countryCode` / `(countryCode, city)` | `countryCode` + `city` indexed | **OK-ish** (group can use indexes; two passes). |
| `people()` (`Catalog+Faces.swift:133`) | `LEFT JOIN faces ON personID`, `GROUP BY p.id`, + per-row `COALESCE` subqueries for cover/representative face | `faces.personID` indexed | **Correlated subqueries** — two per person row (cover-face check + `ORDER BY confidence DESC LIMIT 1`, and `faces.confidence` is unindexed). |
| `unassignedFacesWithEmbeddings` (`Catalog+Faces.swift:112`) | `personID IS NULL AND source='auto'` | `personID` indexed (NULLs), `source` unindexed | **Partial** — then unpacks all U Float16 blobs; feeds the O(U²) clusterer. |
| `librarySize` / `instanceHashes` / `knownHashes` / `assetHashes` (`Queries.swift`, `Catalog.swift`) | `COUNT(*)`/`SUM`/`DISTINCT hash` over full table | none needed / PK | **Full table** by design (aggregate); cheap but O(N/M). |

**Headline gaps for the 100k–1M range:**
1. The **timeline UNION** (`timelineSQL`) is the spine of browse/folder/search, yet every wrapper re-materializes it and re-sorts by `takenAtMs` — the index can't propagate through `SELECT * FROM (… UNION ALL …)`, so all three of `refreshQueries`'s calls pay an O(N+M+D) scan+sort.
2. The **drive-only branch** relies on a **correlated `MIN(rowid)` subquery** for per-asset dedupe (appears in `driveSelect`, `folderCounts`); cost grows with D.
3. **Search predicates** `rating`/`favorite`/`kind`/`cameraModel` and all **tag** queries (`json_each`) have **no index** — Search is a full union scan, and `people()` plus `folderCounts` lean on **correlated subqueries**.

---

## 10. Appendix — Transparency & verification status

**Adversarially refuted (removed from the catalogs above).** Investigation A flagged these but an independent verifier could not confirm them:

- **deleteEmptyFolder hard-deletes .openphoto/ sidecars (data loss, violates never-hard-delete)** (Vault, IO, Hashing, claimed Critical) — The sole caller deleteFolder (AppState+FolderReorg.swift:262) first bins all media recursively, and BinStore.moveToBin (BinStore.swift:29-35) moves each file's .openphoto/<name>.xmp sidecar into the recoverable bin alongside it; deleteEmptyFolder also throws notEmpty (line 40) if any real media file is still physically present, so curated metadata for present assets is never hard-deleted. The only thing lines 43-44 can destroy is a true orphan sidecar (xmp with no media), which the format spec (line 113) and the code itself (VaultReorganizer:89, "stale sidecar... garbage") treat as an invalid/garbage state, so this is at most a minor cleanup wart, not Critical loss of human-authored metadata.
- **embed() deletes the original before moving the rewritten file in — crash-mid-write loses the original** (Scanner, Presence, Media, claimed Critical) — The remove-then-move at lines 69-71 is real and non-atomic (unlike AtomicFile.write's replaceItemAt), but all three callers (Takeout/Photos/Volume sources, via ImportEngine line 86-88) run embed() on a freshly-fetched copy in a UUID-named staging dir, never on the user's source original (src/SD card/Photos library are untouched). A crash mid-write loses only a re-fetchable staging copy inside a do/catch, so no irreplaceable original is destroyed — this is a Low-severity atomicity hardening nit, not a Critical data-loss bug.
- **Per-file scan loops lack autoreleasepool — residual unbounded memory growth (the OOM shape)** (Scanner, Presence, Media, claimed High) — The three dominant memory consumers are already wrapped in autoreleasepool by commit 4cc805f: ContentHash.ofFile pools each 1MB chunk (the ~1.5GB/video driver), and extractImage/EmbeddedMetadata.read pool their ImageIO sources+CFDictionaries — these were the 41GB OOM cause and are fixed. The cited loop-body temporaries are small and mostly ARC-managed Swift natives (URLResourceValues struct, Swift Strings, a tiny JSONEncoder().encode of tags, AssetRecord structs intentionally retained O(N)), not large autoreleased CF/NS buffers; the (entry.path as NSString) bridge is at line 137 in the step-5 instances map, not the extract loop. extractVideo genuinely has no pool but cannot use a synchronous one across its awaits, and its per-file AV loads (duration/naturalSize/a few strings) are small — there is no demonstrated unbounded accumulation of OOM magnitude, making this a Low defensive hardening item (already tracked as task #17), not a confirmed High defect.

**Verification coverage.** Catalog A: every Critical/High verified (3 findings refuted, 17 Highs downgraded). Catalogs B & C: only 2 of 115 findings verified before the spend limit — severities are the auditor's unconfirmed judgement unless marked *Verified*. The scalability/design run is resumable (`resumeFromRunId: wf_64426d9a-063`) to complete verification and the two un-audited UI clusters once the limit resets.
